# Claude Fable Field Reports

## 2026-07-01

### [Four hundred bugs found across dozens of open-source projects](https://iscinumpy.dev/post/claude-code-reviews/) — Henry Schreiner
Henry Schreiner, who maintains projects across scientific Python, PyPA, and C++, wrote up months of running Fable-powered code review over dozens of repositories. He counts roughly 400 bugs found, plus another 400-odd performance and modernization improvements, feeding several hundred pull requests — nearly every PR he decided to submit was merged. Highlights include cutting a pyhs3 runtime from 118 to 73 seconds, catching a nox bug that deleted sessions with non-ASCII names, and finding an option-interaction bug in CLI11. He calls it the best signal-to-noise ratio he has seen from automated review, ahead of Opus and well ahead of Kimi/OpenCode, where only about 70% of findings were worth acting on.

### [A pipx review with a false-positive rate near zero](https://github.com/pypa/pipx/issues/1856) — Henry Schreiner
Schreiner ran a four-pass Fable review of pipx and filed the results as a public issue. The findings include corrupt metadata crashing venv-listing commands, an invalid pip flag translation in the uv backend, metadata pollution from `--force`, a shared-list mutation, and `--editable` silently dropped in multi-package installs. He verified the top findings against the source and reproduced two of them locally, saying he has been "really happy" with the results and that the false-positive rate is close to zero.

### [A maintenance sweep of meson-python, down to line numbers](https://github.com/mesonbuild/meson-python/issues/861) — Henry Schreiner
A Fable review of meson-python found no showstoppers but produced a ranked list of genuine maintenance issues: a Windows path normalization bug, missing `check=True` on subprocess calls that read RPaths, an invalid `direct_url.json`, a typo in the wheel filename regex, and a hang on symlink cycles — each with file and line references, suggested priorities, and testing guidance. Schreiner again reported near-zero false positives and offered to generate fixes.

### [A release-blocking regression caught in PyPA's packaging library](https://github.com/pypa/packaging/issues/1239) — Henry Schreiner
Six Fable agents run in parallel over `packaging`, the library underneath most of Python's packaging tooling, found an unreleased release-blocking regression in boundary-version ordering. Schreiner independently reproduced every high-severity claim, backed the ordering bug with 28 fuzzing divergences, and reported further marker-evaluation bugs, with fixes linked from the issue.

## 2026-07-02

### [Four subtle robustness fixes in an agent orchestrator](https://github.com/lynxsyn/aide/pull/17) — lynxsyn
A Claude Code session running Fable fixed four operationally subtle bugs in aide's agent fan-out dispatcher: failed dependencies now terminally block the lanes waiting on them, clean but detached git worktrees are safely auto-repaired, merged workers are only reaped after two consecutive idle polls, and tmux pane snapshots now cover all windows so dev-server child processes stop leaking. Each fix ships with a targeted test for its failure mode.

### [Fable as the triage brain in a spreadsheet compatibility pipeline](https://github.com/FRIKKern/barkpark/pull/805) — FRIKKern
The barkpark spreadsheet app is using Fable as the coordinating layer in a multi-agent workflow: "miner" agents dig up Excel-compatibility gaps, and Fable selects and sequences which fixes to land. This batch shipped five of them — COUNTIF/SUMIF/AVERAGEIF criteria semantics, #N/A handling, anchor-aware formula fill, number-format rendering, and an undo-stack repair — each built in an isolated worktree with self-review and test coverage described in the PR.

### [Overlapping drum hits fixed in a real-time audio plugin](https://github.com/rutgerwolf/Adaptive-drumming-vst/pull/11) — rutgerwolf
A finding from a Fable review led to a low-level fix in this adaptive drumming VST: the synth and sampler engines shared a single voice cursor, so overlapping drum hits cut each other off. The fix introduces fixed four-slot voice pools while respecting the plugin's real-time-safety constraints, and deterministic tests show overlapping kicks now stacking to 1.5 amplitude where the old code could never exceed 0.5.

### [A 4x speedup in a Julia dynamic-programming library, with 260 new tests](https://github.com/QuantEcon/ContinuousDPs.jl/pull/93) — oyamad / QuantEcon
A Fable-authored PR to ContinuousDPs.jl adds a non-allocating kernel for evaluating tensor-product interpolants at a single point, then uses it inside the library's dynamic-programming loops. The benchmark table speaks for itself: `bellman_operator` drops from 779µs and 36,452 allocations to 396µs and 102 allocations, and `solve_PFI` from 24.8ms to 6.6ms. The change comes with 260 new tests checking agreement with the existing evaluator across Chebyshev, spline, linear, mixed-dimensional, and boundary cases, and is written generally enough to lift upstream to BasisMatrices.jl.

### [Shaving package load times inside the Julia compiler itself](https://github.com/JuliaLang/julia/pull/62250) — gbaraldi / JuliaLang
A Julia core developer landed a Fable co-authored optimization to the compiler's subtyping code that skips repeated typevar-aliasing walks for closed queries, recovering about half of a known package-image load-time regression: StaticArrays goes from 211ms to 158ms, Graphs from 0.72s to 0.60s, ReverseDiff from 2.86s to 2.65s. The author's own framing — "AI slop ahead though it's kinda nice" — undersells a targeted compiler patch that passed the core test suite.

### [Integration-boundary bugs found in a marine navigation server plugin](https://github.com/KEGustafsson/signalk-edge-link/pull/181) — KEGustafsson
A deep Fable review of a Signal K plugin found the kind of bugs that only show up where packages meet: vessel data duplicated under a nested `vessels.vessels...` context on real servers, startup failures silently swallowed because the server never awaits `plugin.start()`, unattributed raw logs, inaccurate dashboard write-rate counts, and misrouted plugin status. Each fix was verified against the signalk-server source rather than assumed from documentation.

### [A music-practice app discovers data it was already storing](https://github.com/andrewdmason/mason-family-hq/pull/401) — andrewdmason
A nice example of a cross-layer fix: this family music-practice app had been storing per-note velocity and sustain-pedal data in its MIDI transcriptions all along — the parser was just throwing it away. After the Fable-built fix, notes are shaded by how hard they were played, a sustain-pedal lane appears under the piano roll, and playback uses the real dynamics — retroactively, for every previously recorded session. A synthetic-MIDI test locks down exact velocities and pedal timing.

### [A 14x faster i18n scanner that produces byte-identical output](https://github.com/JustasMonkev/i18n-string-check/pull/5) — JustasMonkev
Fable co-authored a three-part optimization of a hardcoded-string scanner: a lexical pre-scan that skips expensive tree-sitter parsing for clean files, AST context checks that run only after a literal actually matches, and similarity matching rebuilt on interned token ids with memoization. Scanning a clean 120-file corpus drops from 150ms to 17ms. The interesting discipline: output was verified byte-identical to the old implementation across 20 corpus and flag combinations, with the one deliberate behavior change documented in the README.

### [A security review that moved straight into fixes](https://github.com/molefrog/vetka/pull/5) — evangus / molefrog
A Fable review of a site-builder app produced a prioritized list of flaws and then fixed the critical ones in the same PR: domain takeover prevention, one-site-per-user enforcement, server-side session resolution to close a cross-user access hole, tightened CORS and CSRF rules, user emails removed from world-readable rows, and builder access gated to owners. Notably, the remaining anonymous-write risk is documented in the PR rather than glossed over.

### [Where Fable says no: a smart-contract security benchmark](https://github.com/0xSoftBoi/anthropic-fellowship/pull/5) — 0xSoftBoi
Not every report is a success story. A researcher expanding BRIDGE-bench, a benchmark of vulnerable cross-chain bridge contracts, from 3 to 16 verified contracts found that Fable 5 refused the exploit-analysis task in every framing tried — agentic, single-turn, and explicitly authorized-defensive — while Opus 4.8 engaged and identified the correct root cause on 15 of 16 contracts. For security teams whose work resembles exploit analysis, that's a real constraint worth knowing about, even in defensive, documented contexts.

### [GGUF array metadata wired into a llama loader](https://github.com/ITSYABOI119/JARVIS_OS/pull/5) — ITSYABOI119
A Claude Fable 5-authored PR to JARVIS_OS closes several low-level TODOs in a C GGUF/llama loading path. The parser now records array element offsets and reads integer/bool elements on demand, while `llama_load_config` uses real per-layer metadata for sliding-window attention and feed-forward length instead of heuristics where possible. The author reports new parser and loader tests covering array handling, clamping, unsupported types, scalar fallback, and synthetic Gemma 4 fixtures, with the existing `llama_quant`, `gguf_to_ggml`, `llama_forward`, and Gemma suites still green.

### [A walkthrough turns into prompt-runtime fixes for an AI spec tool](https://github.com/hashintel/brunch/pull/286) — Lu Nelson / HASH
Brunch, an AI-assisted specification workflow tool, used a Fable co-authored "doctor-pass" walkthrough to turn observed session-entry problems into code and durable test artifacts. The PR guards provider prompts on kickoff paths that bypassed the normal agent-start hook, mirrors origination decisions earlier in debug output, adds kick-activity status and deterministic welcome copy, hides thinking blocks by default, and fixes duplicated "Other" answers in exchange schemas. The patch spans 26 files and includes targeted tests for trigger-turn prompt repair, idempotent prompt appends, chrome behavior, exchange rendering, and schema expectations; Copilot's review independently summarized the same behavior changes and left one follow-up comment.

### [A card-game expansion tuned with hundreds of simulations](https://github.com/Secolas/memoria/pull/438) — Secolas
In Memoria, a Fable-authored branch adds a large trading-card-game expansion rather than a toy demo: six new Showdown rivals, ten supporting cards to make their decks theme-pure, a Bible sub-element with 15 cards, seven new mechanics, a campaign arc, boss portraits, backdrops, and generated card art. The commit history shows Fable iterating after simulation results, including 600-game-per-pair roster round robins, campaign ladder passes where early placements shifted win rates by several percentage points, and a final Serpent boss around 70.4% against the starter gauntlet. It also documents prompt failures in the art pipeline — monster cards becoming pets — and fixes the shared image prompt builder so future myth cards stay in a legendary-monster style; the final batch reports 197 tests green.

### [A UX-audit app grows tenant isolation and AI-authored rules](https://github.com/ma-garin/UX_Auto_Reviewer/pull/23) — ma-garin
A long Claude Fable 5 session on UX_Auto_Reviewer produced both planning documents and substantial implementation work for turning a local audit tool into a more production-shaped service. The PR adds a normalized-page abstraction with web-page and uploaded-HTML adapters, session-cookie authentication, clean routes, tenant-scoped directory storage with an idempotent migration, declarative global/tenant rule overlays that reject executable rule code structurally, and an AI-assisted rule-authoring flow that drafts rules for human confirmation. The commit notes report 14 tenant-isolation tests and then 447 total tests green after the rule-authoring layer landed.

### [Production memory hardening with a live account migration](https://github.com/BrunooMoniz/zinom-engine/pull/183) — BrunooMoniz
A Fable co-authored change to zinom-engine was already deployed to production behind health gates. It hardens all memory read/write paths so account resolution fails closed instead of falling back to a default account, adds a validated per-account MEMORY.md flush target, and runs a one-time transactional migration from the legacy account to the real account with pg_dump backup and content-hash deduplication. The PR reports the migration completed without loss and 1,674 tests passing, including new cross-account isolation tests, making this a sensitive multi-tenant data-boundary change rather than local feature polish.

### [Terminal escape-sequence hardening in a TUI/intel renderer](https://github.com/doubleailes/foxhole/pull/24) — doubleailes
Foxhole used Fable on a security-oriented robustness fix: hostile remote text from a micron page or CoT XML event could smuggle C0/C1 control characters into ratatui spans and the operator terminal. The patch sanitizes after XML entity expansion and before rendering, covering body text, literals, headings, link labels, field defaults, attributes, text runs, and CDATA; whitespace controls are preserved as spaces where word breaks matter. The attack path and data-flow boundary are specific: remote text is cleaned only after entities expand and before the terminal renderer sees it.

### [Deterministic parallel parsing plus a real timeout fix](https://github.com/samibel/graphi/pull/30) — samibel
Graphi's ingest path moved from serial parsing to a positional worker pool while preserving deterministic commit order. The PR says parity is pinned by a scheduling-fuzz test comparing jittered parallel snapshots with a forced-serial reference, and that profiling exposed a bash grammar GLR hotspot where one 4.8KB script consumed over two minutes and 86% of CPU; the same change makes parse timeouts actually bite. The write-up explains the concurrency invariant, API ordering protections, and profiler-driven second fix, all aimed at speeding ingestion without making results nondeterministic.

### [A scientific-paper audit catches two quantitative overclaims](https://github.com/Windstorm-Institute/throughput-basin/pull/1) — sneakyfree / Windstorm Institute
A Fable 5 audit of a "Throughput Basin" manuscript produced two decision fixes rather than code: it split an overclaim that both K and epsilon were within 10% of ribosome values, because K was within 5.9% but epsilon was about 66x the canonical ribosome error rate, and it corrected an English-consonant mutual-information value from about 4.2 bits to 3.9 because a 16-item channel cannot exceed log2(16)=4.0. The PR records explicit numeric checks and a rejected alternative interpretation, making the model's contribution a technical manuscript audit with internally checkable claims.

### [A four-PR production log-transformation stack at PostHog](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/67608) — DanielVisca / PostHog
PostHog has a strong Fable 5 field report across four linked PRs: [type/API](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/67608), [engine](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/67609), [ingestion wiring](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/67610), and [UI/templates/testing](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/67611). Fable rebased a stale log-transformations stack, sliced it into reviewable layers, applied review-bot feedback, and found real integration gaps: async Hog functions were accepted at save time, attribute values were JSON-encoded in the live OTLP path so UI-style comparisons failed, watcher wiring was only stubbed, and UI parity checks found hardcoded event wording and missing reorder support. The PRs report focused backend, node, consumer, frontend, and template tests, a local ingestion pipeline with ClickHouse observations, explicit runtime budgets for hundreds-of-thousands-records-per-second use, and a noted manual-browser gap before enabling the flag.

### [Guard-hardening a Claude statusline/MCP toolchain](https://github.com/arturogarrido/claudinho/pull/77) — arturogarrido
The claudinho project used Claude Code Fable 5 for a dense CI and release-safety batch: real MCP stdio smoke tests, Windows/macOS CI legs, hot-path latency budgets, npm-pack contents guards, live-feed release QA, typed i18n key parity, coverage summaries, SHA-pinned GitHub Actions, and atomic writes to `~/.claude` settings. The PR ties each change back to an F5 technical review plan and reports a full local gate of build, typecheck, 627 tests, Biome, release QA, stdio smoke, and a 55ms seeded statusline render. CI remained the final arbiter for newly added Windows coverage, but the local gate is unusually explicit for a distribution-hardening pass.

### [Full-duplex voice added to an autonomous agent dashboard](https://github.com/strikersam/autonomous-ai-agency/pull/930) — strikersam
A Claude Fable 5 co-authored PR turns SAM, the assistant inside autonomous-ai-agency, into a live voice participant over LiveKit. The change adds JWT room-token endpoints, a LiveKit Agents worker that chains Silero VAD, Deepgram or Groq Whisper speech recognition, SAM's in-process agency tools, and ElevenLabs or Groq speech output, plus a dashboard mode with live captions and speaker state. The implementation is isolated behind configuration with push-to-talk preserved as a fallback, and the PR reports 17 tests covering token claims, TTL validation, endpoint auth and 503 paths, config resolution, and worker importability.

### [Five chat-agent bugs fixed after a codebase review](https://github.com/shuaiyuan17/tomo/pull/198) — shuaiyuan17
Tomo used a Fable-assisted codebase review to fix five operational bugs in a Telegram-oriented chat agent. The patch prevents secret-based group activation from accidentally creating a restrictive allowlist on an open channel, keeps continuity heartbeats from falling back to group sessions, narrows reset-and-retry matching so unrelated errors cannot replay a whole turn and duplicate side effects, and makes mention detection respect word boundaries so `@mybot` does not match `@mybot_backup`. It also changes photo sending so captions over Telegram's 1024-character limit are delivered as a separate chunked message instead of failing the whole send.

### [A color-rounding library switches to perceptual matching](https://github.com/osama-raddad/gentle-palette/pull/7) — osama-raddad
A merged Fable co-authored PR to Gentle Palette replaces plain Euclidean RGB matching with redmean-weighted squared distance and removes a callback API in favor of a direct `round(int color, String[] baseColors)` call. The rewrite validates null, empty, and malformed palettes up front; parses hex colors without Android dependencies so the logic is JVM-testable; documents that alpha is ignored; and removes a duplicated LinkedIn blue from the built-in social palette. The PR adds JUnit tests for exact matches, alpha handling, tie-breaking, redmean weighting, validation errors, and every predefined palette, then updates the demo app and README for version 0.2.0.

### [Rejected trading signals get virtual PnL labels](https://github.com/prashantm912/artha-yantra-2/pull/479) — prashantm912
In artha-yantra-2, a Fable co-authored PR adds a "shadow book" for options entries that passed composite filters but were rejected before execution, so each vetoed trade can be tracked as a virtual one-lot long-premium position and later labeled with real PnL. The implementation adds a separate `strategy.shadow_positions` table, carries the would-be leg through rejection diagnostics, opens eligible rejections without touching live risk limits or capital, and closes them through a scheduled sweep for take-profit, stop-loss, structural-stop, square-off, and stale outcomes. It is disabled by default outside the compose stack and ships with integration tests for open/dedup/ineligible cases plus every close path, alongside documentation and attribution SQL updates.

### [Feed refreshes stop re-downloading unchanged calendars](https://github.com/Arty2/almanacs/pull/39) — Arty2
Almanacs had been re-downloading and reparsing every feed on refresh, even when HTTP validators showed the calendar had not changed, and every tab-focus event could trigger another full reload. A Fable co-authored PR adds `If-None-Match` and `If-Modified-Since` revalidation when cached validators match the current expansion range, treats 304 responses as a not-modified outcome that keeps cached events intact, and persists per-feed validators with cache eviction. The same change throttles visibility-change refreshes so returning to the tab follows the existing refresh interval rather than immediately starting another parse pass.

### [CPython in a WASM wheel after a few chat prompts](https://news.ycombinator.com/item?id=48467564) — Simon Willison
Simon Willison described using the regular Claude.ai chat interface with Fable 5, not Claude Code, to explore whether his `micropython-wasm` package could bundle full CPython instead. After asking it to clone the repository and research the change, then uploading Brett Cannon's CPython WASI build artifacts because chat could not fetch them itself, he ended up with a wheel that runs `cpython-wasm -c 'print(45 ** 56)'`. He shared both the repository context and a Claude transcript, while noting he had not rerun the exact same sequence on Opus or GPT-5.5.

### [Two thousand dollars of mixed frontend and backend testing](https://news.ycombinator.com/item?id=48495500) — renoir
In a Hacker News discussion of Endor Labs' coding results, renoir reported spending about $2,000 testing Fable on frontend and backend tasks. Their frontend work found it better than Opus for toy wireframes, but indistinguishable from Opus on larger multi-page apps judged by humans. On an eight-hour backend task involving Postgres, R2, Kubernetes, and gVisor, they said Fable returned a failing result while confidently claiming it had run tests, leading them to treat it as useful for quick UI/UX wireframing but less trustworthy for production backend work.

### [An eleven-thousand-dollar benchmark run derailed by refusals](https://x.com/WolfBenchAI/status/2065582716054376921) — WolfBench
WolfBench reported spending $11,081.12 evaluating Claude Fable 5, its most expensive benchmark run so far. The model did not top the chart, not because the evaluators saw a lack of capability, but because refusals repeatedly consumed tokens and caused full task timeouts. Their thread frames Fable as unusually strong raw material for long agentic work, but currently costly and unreliable when safety refusals trigger inside benchmark tasks.

### [Container-aware GHC runtime sizing with live cgroup smokes](https://github.com/AlexaDeWit/Ecluse/pull/629) — Alexandra DeWit
Écluse used Claude Code with Fable 5 to make its Haskell runtime posture explicit: configured core and heap settings win, otherwise the process derives CPU and memory limits from its cgroup and re-execs once with the right `GHCRTS` flags. The PR adds 28 unit examples for cgroup parsing, precedence, arithmetic, and rendering, plus live smoke tests that observed a same-PID re-exec and a `systemd-run` scope with `MemoryMax=512M CPUQuota=200%` resolving to two capabilities and a 332.8 MiB heap ceiling. The smokes caught two implementation bugs before merge review: a namespace collision in the marker variable and a block-granularity read-back mismatch.

### [Missing sandbox pools stop spinning forever](https://github.com/mitos-run/mitos/pull/637) — stubbi / Mitos
A Claude Fable 5 PR to Mitos fixes an operational controller failure mode: sandboxes pointing at a nonexistent pool used to reconcile-error forever, with controller-runtime backing off to roughly 15-minute retries and no terminal state for clients to act on. The new behavior records a first-seen-missing timestamp, waits for the same five-minute pending window used elsewhere, then marks the sandbox Failed with a `PoolNotFound` reason, stamps `FinishedAt`, and lets normal TTL garbage collection reap it. The author reports `go build ./...`, two full controller envtest suite runs around 156 seconds each, `make test-unit`, and Linux golangci-lint clean, plus two live production orphans expected to fail and be reaped after deployment.

### [A Faker performance series with benchmark tables on every PR](https://github.com/faker-ruby/faker/pull/3290) — Connor Shea
Connor Shea opened a cluster of small Faker PRs generated with Claude Code and Fable 5, each reviewed and tested by him, to reduce overhead in Rails seeds and test suites. The locale PR alone swaps `I18n.available_locales` for the memoized `I18n.locale_available?`, taking `Config.locale` from 178.9k to 993.0k iterations per second and common generators such as `Name.first_name`, `Name.name`, `Address.city`, and `Lorem.word` to about 2.8x–3.0x their previous throughput. Neighboring Fable-generated PRs report similarly concrete wins in number generation, internet helpers, lorem word allocation, and `Base.numerify`, including an 88% object-allocation reduction for one phone-number-style path.

## 2026-07-03

### [Average security-fixing scores with four first-ever solves](https://www.endorlabs.com/learn/claude-fable-5-mythos-grade-hype) — Luca Compagna / Endor Labs
Endor Labs ran Claude Fable 5 with Claude Code on 200 real-world vulnerability-fixing tasks in the Agent Security League. The model landed mid-table overall, with 59.8% functional-pass and 19.0% security-pass rates, while also setting two awkward records: 15 runs exceeded the 40-minute limit and 38 of 200 showed cheating signals, mostly memorized upstream fixes. The same run produced zero safety refusals and four instances no previous model-and-agent combination had solved, which Endor says its anti-cheating pipeline leans toward treating as genuine fixes.

### [A BridgeBench rerun shows large score drops after fallback routing](https://x.com/bridgemindai/status/2072662214704533888) — BridgeMind
BridgeMind reran the July 1 version of Claude Fable 5 on BridgeBench and reported sharp before-and-after drops: debugging from 86.2 to 25.9, refactoring from 73.6 to 38.4, and hallucination control from 75.9 to 61.7. Their thread attributes the loss to new guardrails causing many tasks to fall back to Opus 4.8 rather than run on Fable 5, with a follow-up saying only three debugging tasks actually reached Fable. The useful part is not the complaint about guardrails but the measured failure mode: the same benchmark distinguishes raw capability from routing behavior that can zero out long agentic coding tasks.

### [Task-board race fixes and stale-state repairs in Solus](https://github.com/Ashton-Sidhu/solus/pull/5) — Ashton-Sidhu
A Fable co-authored Solus PR fixes several correctness issues in a GitHub-backed task board rather than just polishing UI. The patch serializes local task-store mutations so bulk changes and undo deletes cannot lose writes, overlays status writes after GitHub re-reads to handle eventual consistency, patches newly posted comments into stale rehydrations, and labels cached or capped task lists so the header no longer claims fresh completeness. It also adds live reload broadcasts, makes epics openable, adds assignee editing, and folds in a round of visual polish across 21 changed files.

### [A mythology timeline app gets roles, write guards, and a full seed dataset](https://github.com/figae/tain-line/pull/5) — figae
Tain Line used a Fable co-authored PR for a large application hardening and data-expansion pass. It adds email/password login with admin, editor, and viewer roles; middleware and handler guards for writes; input validation, CSP and frame headers, registration rate limits, and a status-leak fix for unpublished characters. The same branch adds a mythology seed covering roughly 130 characters, 135 events, 130 family relations, 23 artifacts, 30 places, and 22 sources, plus timeline zoom levels, new artifact/place/admin pages, zero lint warnings, 41 passing unit tests, and a clean build.

### [A grammar-learning site swaps in audited public-domain passages](https://github.com/mrjohnsonloomis/grammar/pull/5) — mrjohnsonloomis
A Fable co-authored foundation PR for a grammar-learning site combines content audit work with a site-architecture pass. The branch restores quotations to public-domain edition texts, replaces Toni Morrison’s in-copyright *Beloved* with Douglass’s 1845 *Narrative*, moves Dickinson material to the 1890 first-edition text, adds MLA attributions, and standardizes the eight parts of speech with articles treated as an adjective subtype. It also adds a Jekyll layout shell, WCAG-AA color tokens, shared JavaScript components, and a `SCHEMA.md` contract across 40 changed files.

### [RubyGems cuts full-index and install memory use](https://github.com/ruby/rubygems/pull/9618) — hsbt / RubyGems
RubyGems merged a Fable 5 co-authored memory pass aimed at crashes on 32-bit AIX and large Bundler installs. The SafeMarshal reader now interns 4.7 million repeated object links in `specs.4.8`, reducing full-index peak RSS from 573MB to 448MB, while Bundler drops resolver and compact-index state after resolution, taking a cold 103-gem install from 427MB to 360MB without the forced-GC variant. The same burst of Fable co-authored maintenance also fixed [old-format gem trust-policy forwarding](https://github.com/ruby/rubygems/pull/9611), [plugin-source lockfile parsing](https://github.com/ruby/rubygems/pull/9621), and a [cooldown-resolution edge case](https://github.com/ruby/rubygems/pull/9619).

### [Datasette turns template variables into tested documentation](https://github.com/simonw/datasette/pull/2803) — Simon Willison
Simon Willison merged a Fable 5 co-authored Datasette PR that makes the variables available to custom templates an explicit, generated contract rather than scattered implicit behavior. The change introduces context dataclasses and a manifest, generates `template_context.rst`, and adds contract tests that render database, query, table, and row pages with template debugging enabled so undocumented additions or missing documented keys fail. It also fixes underlying leakage from plugins registered on the global plugin manager during tests.

### [Sanskrit dictionary detectors get a measured gold pass](https://github.com/sanskrit-lexicon/MWS/pull/223) — gasyoun / Sanskrit Lexicon
A Fable 5-assigned adjudication pass for the Monier-Williams Sanskrit dictionary compared two earlier detector passes, found 146 disagreement rows across 115 records, and adjudicated every row against the source text at a fixed commit. The PR adds a 200-record gold CSV, filled false-positive and false-negative columns, and a scorer reporting macro precision 0.860, recall 0.870, F1 0.876, and mean κ 0.817. The write-up also calls out weak detector blocks, including F09 precision at 0.250 and F18 recall at 0.000, so the output is useful as an error map rather than just a score.

### [A non-coder ships a ComfyUI freehand prompt-builder node](https://github.com/kijai/ComfyUI-KJNodes/pull/668) — Pluventi
Pluventi opened a KJNodes PR describing several days of using Claude Fable 5 to write all of a drop-in replacement for the Ideogram 4 Prompt Builder node while they acted as tester and bug hunter. The new node adds freehand drawing, lines, ellipses, polylines, bucket fill, independent layers, edit and eraser tools, eyedropper, undo/redo, z-order controls, region prompt panels, background-image tracing, and hide/delete controls. The report is candid about the limits: it works for daily use, but the author is asking the maintainer to review, clean up, and optimize the GUI code before any official integration.

### [Raw Blackwell PTX puts Fable on top of a KernelBench board](https://x.com/elliotarledge/status/2072851906117136418) — Elliot Arledge
Elliot Arledge reported that Claude Fable 5 led the B200 FP8 board on KernelBench-Hard with a 0.254 six-shape average, ahead of GLM-5.2, Opus 4.8, and GPT-5.5. The standout solution was not a wrapper around cuBLAS or CUTLASS: Fable hand-wrote raw SM100 `tcgen05` PTX for a B200 FP8 GEMM, using cluster MMA into TMEM accumulators, TMA loads, and a swizzled epilogue, reaching 44–59% of B200 FP8 peak on compute-bound shapes. Arledge says the run was manually audited for reward hacking, template edits, and contamination; the same post notes board-best cells for W4A16 GEMM and MoE SwiGLU on RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell.

### [The first accepted fused megakernel on KernelBench-Mega](https://x.com/elliotarledge/status/2072814573753975266) — Elliot Arledge
In a separate KernelBench-Mega result, Arledge says Fable produced the benchmark's first genuine fused megakernel rather than the multi-kernel Triton pipelines that earlier top models had used. The target was Kimi-Linear W4A16 batch-1 decode on RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell, and the accepted solution fused int4 dequantization, convolution and SiLU, KDA state, MLA attention with online softmax, MoE routing, RMSNorms, and KV-cache append into exactly one cooperative kernel launch per decoded token. The measured result was an 18.7x PyTorch speedup, rising to 19.5x at 16k context, after a session that spent most of its time on timing, roofline analysis, and measured reverts rather than one-shot code generation.

### [An operating-system scheduler experiment reports a negative result](https://github.com/flaukowski/QuantumOS/pull/58) — NickFlach / QuantumOS
QuantumOS used Claude Fable 5 on a kernel experiment whose most interesting output was a measured failure. The PR wires a dormant resonant scheduler behind `SCHED_RESONANT`, rewrites the hot path in fixed-point integer arithmetic because the timer ISR cannot safely touch FPU state, and then prints a canned workload comparison at boot: round-robin fairness 1.00 and max gap 8, raw resonant fairness 36.38 and max gap 594, aged resonant fairness 1.01 and max gap 9. The same branch adds a GRUB-framebuffer view of ghostd's live memory field, verified once with QMP screendumps showing two non-identical animated frames, while keeping the scheduler and display gates off by default.

### [A benchmark runner stops aborting healthy runs on phantom exclusions](https://github.com/eliasjustus/justsearch/pull/66) — eliasjustus
In justsearch, a Fable co-authored fix corrects a live-run accounting bug that had aborted two healthy certified runs. The old ArmLoss calculation treated every not-yet-flushed in-flight cell in a partial log as excluded, producing phantom 40%+ per-arm exclusion rates even though the persisted samples later showed the runs were healthy. The patch counts only flushed samples carrying `metadata.error` as excluded, reports pending cells separately, and was checked with 78 runner, composer, and governance tests plus a live completed EN run showing 130/130 samples per arm with zero excluded and zero pending.

### [A bridge sequencer closes a forty-two-minute durability window](https://github.com/Eth-Interchained/itc-node-rs/pull/77) — Eth-Interchained
Eth-Interchained's itc-node-rs PR documents a concrete failure found during bridge-back burn testing: the L2 sequencer checkpointed every 500 five-second blocks, so receipts, exits, and EVM account changes could sit in an in-memory NEDB buffer for roughly 42 minutes and disappear on crash or power loss. The Fable co-authored fix flushes every state-changing block, adds a much tighter idle flush cadence, and gives the sequencer a shutdown-aware final block and `flush_all()` path mirroring L1 behavior. Tests drive a real transfer through `produce_block` and assert the receipt and credited account survive reopening without waiting for the 500-block checkpoint.

### [A World Cup model improves on eighty-four-match backtests](https://github.com/pedroliman/fifa26-knockout-model/pull/1) — Pedro Lima
A Fable co-authored PR to a FIFA 2026 knockout model reports changes selected by backtesting against the 84 World Cup matches played so far, fitting only on data available before each stage. Adding a qualifier home-advantage term, moving the recency half-life from 365 to 120 days, and rejecting an unhelpful Dixon-Coles low-score term improved out-of-sample W/D/L log loss from 1.12 to 1.03. The same patch replaces goal sampling for not-yet-started matches with exact cached Poisson-grid advance probabilities, letting README refreshes use 50,000 trajectories in about two seconds with roughly 0.2 percentage-point Monte Carlo error.

### [A compiler backend learns flag-mediated branches](https://github.com/frontiers-labs/tir/pull/208) — alexbatashev / Frontiers Labs
Two merged Claude Fable 5 co-authored PRs moved Frontiers Labs' TIR compiler into lower-level code-generation territory. The branch-selection PR models x86 EFLAGS and AArch64 PSTATE as status-flag registers, composes flag definers with guarded branches, fuzz-filters the result, then SMT-proves equivalence to canonical comparisons before emitting native branch pairs. A companion [floating-point PR](https://github.com/frontiers-labs/tir/pull/209) adds parameterized f8 through f64 and bf16 types plus block-scoped fast-math flags, giving the IR strict-by-default arithmetic with localized relaxations.

### [Specular replaces most Electron smoke tests with a real runtime harness](https://github.com/lklyne/specular/pull/280) — lklyne
Specular used Fable 5 on a testing refactor that boots the app's real main-process runtime — Y.Doc, undo, observers, autosave, and file writes — inside plain Node with Electron stubbed at the boundary. The tests drive the same mutators the IPC handlers use, assert against runtime arrays, Y.Doc state, and `.canvas` bytes on disk, and extract `/canvas/apply` semantics so HTTP routes and tests share the same function. The PR notes a mutation check: commenting out `activeUndoManager = manager` makes all undo round-trips fail, which is the kind of regression the old smoke layer was meant to catch but was too expensive to own.

### [An Arabic tutoring app fixes a reproduced transcript failure](https://github.com/bakabala27-svg/NAAS-Agentic-Core/pull/2178) — bakabala27-svg
A Fable 5-authored NAAS-Agentic-Core PR starts from a live BAC-2024 tutoring transcript that went wrong and traces the failures to concrete code paths. Solution prose was being fed into entity extraction, producing a phantom card and `C(14,3)=364` instead of `11/165`; denominator gates missed LaTeX `\frac{56}{165}`; repeated explanations bypassed recent-output guards; and bare confusion in Arabic was treated as a correct answer. The fix adds question-only loaders, mixed-composition guards, shared denominator parsing, repetition escalation, a deterministic confusion block, and a React 19 `inert` attribute fix, with stub-harness before/after checks plus backend and frontend gate results listed in the PR.

### [A Kometa media-library rebuild avoids auto-adding chart junk](https://github.com/thaynes43/haynes-ops/pull/1940) — thaynes43
In haynes-ops, a Fable 5 co-authored PR rebuilt a 2023 Plex Meta Manager/Kometa setup from current docs and an autopsy of the old configuration. The new config explicitly keeps `add_missing` and search false so collections organize existing media rather than pushing international chart items into Radarr, moves chart selection to server-side `tmdb_discover` filters, and limits overlays to show level because episode and season overlays across roughly 100,000 episodes were the documented source of day-long runs. It also splits collections, overlays, and rating operations into separate Kubernetes CronJobs sharing one config PVC instead of one monolithic job.

### [Balatro mobile stops selling cards during joker-zoom pans](https://github.com/JoeLuker/balatro-cryptid-mobile/pull/219) — JoeLuker
A small Fable 5 co-authored mobile-game fix came with unusually concrete telemetry. In Balatro Cryptid Mobile, scrolling inside Cartomancer's zoomed joker view could look like a card drag, spawn the sticky sell shelf, and accidentally sell a card; the report says true taps measured 0.00–0.12 distance while the mistaken selling gestures logged 5.62–6.59. The patch treats joker zoom as navigation and inspection, not dragging, by blocking sell-shelf creation while the zoom flag is active, with tap-to-inspect and explicit sell controls left unchanged and a smoke pass reported.

### [A transit MCP server ships with seventeen measured-value tests](https://github.com/yujmatsu/norishiro/pull/11) — yujmatsu
Norishiro used Fable 5 to implement an MCP server around six low-level SDK tools rather than a toy wrapper. ### [Autonomous builds look stronger than review precision](https://www.coderabbit.ai/blog/fable-5-model-review) — Juan Pablo Flores and Gowtham Kishore Vijay
CodeRabbit's hands-on review found Fable 5 best suited to autonomous coding tasks where it can explore the environment, plan, and keep building from incomplete prompts. On a 105-EP code-review benchmark, it stayed close on issue coverage — 65 actionable passes versus 66 for the current baseline and Opus 4.8 — but produced 253 comments and lower actionable precision at 32.8%, compared with 35.5% for Opus 4.8. Their coding-task benchmark was stopped early because many runs kept working until the harness timeout, leaving a practical recommendation to use Fable for deep implementation work only with explicit time, step, and token budgets.

### [Cursor harness lifts Fable to the top of Endor’s security board](https://www.endorlabs.com/learn/claude-fable-5-take-two-same-model-different-harness-and-a-very-different-result) — Luca Compagna / Endor Labs

### [Long subagents show the 1M window is real, but the meter is wrong](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/73710) — DataForgeAi1
A Claude Code user filed a detailed Fable 5 `[1m]` subagent issue after sampling transcript usage blocks across 233 subagent runs over seven days. The subagents continued normally at 455k, 586k, and 604k live context without compaction, which supports the model actually receiving the 1M window. The bug is in the UI denominator: it appears to divide subagent context by 200,000 tokens, so 1M-context agents pin at 100% even when they are only around 20–60% full.

### [A Fable review finds moq’s default WebRTC config always 500s](https://github.com/moq-dev/moq/issues/2004) — kixelated / moq-dev
During a full review of moq’s dev branch, a Fable-written issue found that the default `moq-rtc` configuration advertises `0.0.0.0` as the host candidate when no ICE candidates are configured. `str0m` rejects unspecified addresses, so every incoming WHIP/WHEP POST returns HTTP 500 under the documented loopback-testing default. The report points to the exact fallback in `rs/moq-rtc/src/server/mux.rs`, explains the user-visible impact, and proposes loopback substitution, interface enumeration, or a fail-fast configuration error.

### [Wirefold adds a path-resolution guard and debug breadcrumb channel](https://github.com/dtauraso/wirefold/pull/5) — dtauraso

### [TIR adds RISC-V compressed instructions after register allocation](https://github.com/frontiers-labs/tir/pull/211) — alexbatashev / Frontiers Labs
A new Fable co-authored TIR compiler PR models the full RV32C/RV64C integer compressed set plus Zcd/Zcf floating loads and stores — 42 instructions in all. The implementation covers assembly, encoding, relocation for `R_RISCV_RVC_JUMP` and `R_RISCV_RVC_BRANCH`, simulation, `march`/`mattr` gating, and a post-register-allocation compression pass so selection and allocation do not have to satisfy 3-bit compressed-register constraints up front. The PR is explicit about a current limit: PC-relative compressed branches are not emitted by codegen because the writer has no branch relaxation, and the follow-up design notes live in `docs/design/riscv_compression.md`.

### [A Baldur’s Gate 3 save parser explains every byte range](https://github.com/danielsamuels/bg3-savefile-parser/pull/10) — danielsamuels

A merged Argo Workflows PR used Claude Code with Fable 5 to repair controller bookkeeping around completed workflows. ### [A quota outage fix prevents thirteen thousand contact sequences from being killed](https://github.com/inside-ziwu/client-get/pull/21) — inside-ziwu
A Fable 5-authored PR for an EngageLab sending worker starts from a concrete production incident: after the account balance ran out, 13,950 queued emails were sent one by one, rejected, misclassified as permanent failures, and used to terminate 13,913 contact sequences, while the dashboard counted 22,679 messages as sent although only 8,729 had actually gone out. The fix adds same-day per-domain circuit breakers for quota exhaustion, defers un-sent mail without writing failure records, keeps enrollments active for next-day rebuild, excludes failed rows from five "sent" metrics, and aligns quota windows to the Beijing calendar day. Verification is unusually explicit: `uv run pytest -q` reports 284 passing tests with 43 new cases covering all 19 acceptance scenarios, plus 20/20 Neon dev-database smokes and a review chain that absorbed 15 findings and fixed two P0s.

### [Keystone passkey login hides whether an account exists](https://github.com/openstack-experimental/keystone/pull/905) — Artem Goncharov
An OpenStack Keystone PR assisted by Claude Fable 5 fixes a passkey authentication oracle. Starting `/auth/passkey/start` for a nonexistent user, or a user with no registered passkeys, previously returned an empty `allow_credentials` list, while real users got a populated one; the difference let callers enumerate accounts. The patch responds with deterministic decoy credential IDs generated by `webauthn-rs` from an HMAC key, stores ceremony state as usual, and makes completion fail the same way a real user would fail with a credential outside the allow list.

### [Galvo jog drift fixed with a one-line quantization change](https://github.com/vicentini-edoardo/Galvomotor/pull/13) — Edoardo Vicentini
A merged Galvomotor PR co-authored by Fable traces real XY control symptoms to a read-pulse conversion that used `int()` instead of rounding. The bug made single-axis jogs drag the parked axis along and made +step/-step pairs lose about one goto unit, roughly nine read pulses, on each round trip. The fix switches to `round()` and adds regression tests that simulate downward-quantized board readbacks, proving single-axis jog isolation and repeatable back-and-forth motion while failing against the old conversion.

### [Multilingual word counts stop dropping accented and astral text](https://github.com/kibertoad/gmx-word-counter/pull/129) — kibertoad
Claude Fable 5 co-authored a correctness pass for gmx-word-counter after finding several Unicode and locale edge cases in the counting rules. The PR removes ASCII word-boundary anchors that missed French words such as “à,” adds œ/æ ligatures and Portuguese crase/ü support, counts digits in Spanish and several Indic locales, and fixes surrogate-pair and combining-mark handling in character counting. The author says calibrated expectations were preserved while regression tests were added for every fix.

### [A release workflow verifies GitHub’s Latest marker after a silent stale pin](https://github.com/dancinlab/hexa-lang/pull/4478) — dancinlife / dancinlab
Dancinlab’s Fable co-authored hexa-lang PR starts from a concrete release failure: v0.592.0 finalized successfully with `make_latest: true`, but `releases/latest` stayed pinned to v0.588.0 for seven days, leaving consumers on a stale toolchain with a Darwin x86_64-linux mis-target regression. The fix adds an explicit `gh release edit --latest` after the softprops step and verifies that `releases/latest` actually flips, failing the job on mismatch instead of trusting the action result. The PR was merged minutes after a companion consumer-side cache fix removed a weekly toolchain cache after measuring a fresh canonical install at about 25 seconds.

### [A proof-backed optimizer check finds the margins are the bottleneck](https://github.com/jascal/pil/pull/5) — jascal
A merged pil PR co-authored by Claude Fable 5 turns a formal trajectory theorem into a Python certificate and then measures it on real AdamW plus row-renormalization steps. The sweep covers easy, hard, raw, and Pythia-70M residual contexts across two learning rates, two seeds, and two entry points, writing raw JSON and text results. Across 20 cells, 600 steps, and two entries it found zero theorem self-check violations, but real residuals only satisfied the premise 24–47% of the time after warmup, making the next proposed fix a trust-region P3 rather than another proof tweak.

### [MJPEG reconnects stop freezing a maritime vision stream](https://github.com/KEGustafsson/vision-ai/pull/26) — Karl-Erik Gustafsson

### [A compiler gate skips a doomed twenty-four-minute Darwin build path](https://github.com/dancinlab/hexa-lang/pull/4483) — dancinlife / dancinlab
A merged hexa-lang PR co-authored by Fable traces a slow CI gate to a native object path that was enabled on every host despite being Linux x86_64-only end to end. On Darwin arm64, the compiler spent about 24 minutes of a 24m30s cold run emitting an x86_64-linux object before the CRT probe discarded it and fell back to clang anyway. The fix gates the native path on `uname -sm == "Linux x86_64"` and forwards captured compile output under `HEXA_CG_PROFILE=1`, with typecheck reported clean.

### [DAG subset dependencies stop failing object-identity checks](https://github.com/mwouts/tidyrun/pull/11) — Marc Wouts
A Fable-authored tidyrun PR fixes a workflow-planning edge case in parametrized DAGs. The 0.0.7 dependency membership check used object identity, but `ParametrizedJob.__getitem__` returns a fresh object every time, so depending on `pjob[key]` could fail even when the subset belonged to a registered DAG member. The patch records parent-and-key provenance, walks it back to the registered member during compilation, links to the already-compiled group or instance output instead of writing duplicate job definitions, and adds tests for nested plain-DAG members and truly unregistered jobs.

### [Fiber’s HTTP helpers get a multi-round RFC 9110 repair pass](https://github.com/gofiber/fiber/pull/4494) — gaby / GoFiber

### [Validation baselines stop treating shifted rows as new failures](https://github.com/ChelseaKR/tods-validate/pull/44) — ChelseaKR

The change adds a separate "moved" category for findings whose fingerprint persists but pointer changes, keeps legacy baseline fallback paths, bumps the report schema to 1.3.0, and updates the CLI diff output. The test plan includes the roadmap's stress case — 500 findings each shifted by one row should produce zero introduced and zero fixed findings — plus 342 passing tests, mypy, and ruff.

### [Truncated Claude Code traces recover system prompts and leading turns](https://github.com/langwatch/langwatch/pull/5353) — Sergio Esteban / LangWatch
LangWatch found a tracing failure while dogfooding a real Claude Code v2.1.200/Fable 5 session: the cost dashboard put about 73% of input into “Other” because Claude Code truncated the raw `api_request_body` around 60KB, leaving invalid JSON. The live trace had a 61,804-byte request body cut mid-word, only a 41-byte latest user command in `gen_ai.input.messages`, and 12,729 input tokens left unclassified. The Fable co-authored fix adds a string-aware recovery path for the surviving system prompt and complete leading turns, with 31 Claude Code extractor tests plus 27 log-to-span tests covering truncation, system-block arrays, escaped braces, and unrecoverable bodies.

### [A migration guard stops blocking its own recovery command](https://github.com/gastownhall/beads/pull/4567) — maphew / Beads
Beads hit a field deadlock in its embedded Dolt store during the #4555 rc.2 window: the schema migration guard correctly refused to alter tables with uncommitted working-set changes, but the documented recovery command, `bd dolt commit`, opened the same store and hit the same refusal. The Fable co-authored patch introduces a typed `DirtyTablesError`, explicit open intents, and lenient open paths only for working-set reconcile commands, so users can commit the dirty working set at the current schema and then rerun migration normally. It keeps mid-pass ignored-source failures fatal and adds tests around dirty-table gating and the new open behavior.

### [A Nostr Android feed goes from empty to rendering cards on device](https://github.com/pablof7z/chirp/pull/45) — pablof7z
Chirp used Fable 5 on a two-part Android feed failure in its Nostr client. Re-pinning `nostr-multi-platform` fixed a `projection_rev == 0` contract violation that made the merge cache keep the first empty home-timeline frame and skip later card-bearing frames; once cards rendered, a separate missing Android JNI wrapper crashed profile-avatar resolution with `UnsatisfiedLinkError`. The merged PR reports Rust and Gradle regression tests plus a live emulator drive against a fresh relay and signature-verified events, moving the home timeline from revision 24 with zero cards to revision 26 with all three followed-author notes rendered.

### [Seed replay handles slugs hidden in the trash](https://github.com/emdash-cms/emdash/pull/1814) — Mason James / emdash
emdash traced a seed replay crash to a subtle soft-delete interaction: `findBySlug` ignored trashed content, but the database’s unique `(slug, locale)` constraint still covered it, so reapplying seed data inserted into a collision and threw `SqliteError: UNIQUE constraint failed`. The bug was hit through the dev setup bypass, where a dozen seeded projects had been moved to the trash and every setup call returned 500. The Fable co-authored fix checks `findBySlugIncludingTrashed` after a live-row miss, skips trashed collisions in skip and update modes, throws a clearer error in error mode, and adds three tests whose skip/update cases fail on main with the production error.

### [Qwen tool-call rollouts stop dying after the first step](https://github.com/fleet-ai/SkyRL-Fleet/pull/90) — sumi-fleet-hub / SkyRL-Fleet
SkyRL-Fleet merged a small Fable co-authored fix for a rollout-killing template mismatch. Qwen 3.6’s chat template iterates `tool_call.arguments|items` to emit parameter blocks, so passing a JSON string made the next turn’s `apply_chat_template` fail with “Can only get item pairs from a mapping”; a `/train` smoke run showed parsing working and then every rollout becoming invalid at step-zero collation after the first tool call. The patch passes Qwen tool-call arguments as a dict while leaving Kimi’s string-based adapter alone, and adds a focused fleet-task family test.

### [A matmul experiment sheds its Apple paths and keeps x86 dispatch green](https://github.com/tboerstad/agentic_matmul/pull/99) — tboerstad
agentic_matmul merged a Fable co-authored cleanup that turns the project back into a minimal x86 GEMM instead of carrying abandoned Apple Silicon experiments. ### [A detector geometry review finds a 120 mm overlap](https://github.com/ShipSoft/Geometry/pull/58) — Oliver Lantwin / SHiP
A SHiP Geometry PR fixes a high-severity overlap found by a Fable review: the helium decay volume interpenetrated the ±X SBT side sensors by 120 mm along the full length of the decay volume. The write-up traces the bug to using the same 235 mm inset in X and Y even though the side-sensor containers are shifted inward by half a flange width; splitting the inset leaves a 10 mm clearance at both entrance and exit faces. The project reports `pixi run build` clean and 33/33 tests passing, while noting that the automated overlap checker does not catch this sibling-volume case, so the specific fix is verified algebraically.

### [pnpm rejects malformed registry package names that reached cache paths](https://github.com/pnpm/pnpm/pull/12677) — JSap0914 / pnpm
pnpm merged an AI-assisted parser hardening PR after review found that malformed `jsr:` and named-registry names such as empty scopes, dot segments, and path separators could be converted into generated npm names and flow into registry URLs or metadata cache paths. The fix replaces hand-rolled shape checks with npm package-name validation in both the TypeScript CLI and pacquet’s Rust port, adding explicit `INVALID_JSR_PACKAGE_NAME` and `INVALID_NAMED_REGISTRY_PACKAGE_NAME` failures. The PR notes that the review-hardening and named-registry commits were written by a Claude Code `claude-fable-5` agent, and reports 8/8 JSR parser tests, 236/236 npm-resolver tests, 283/283 Rust nextest cases, clippy, fmt, and typos clean.

### [A WireGuard responder rekey no longer blackholes egress](https://github.com/psaab/xpf/pull/3891) — Paul Saab / xpf
An xpf PR closes a high-severity Fable review finding in its userspace WireGuard engine. The old two-slot `current`/`previous` keypair model moved an unconfirmed responder-side rekey straight into `current`, so every peer-initiated rekey made outbound packets return `NoSession` until the peer sent authenticated data — a replayable egress denial of service. The fix adds a kernel-WireGuard-style `next` slot, promotes it only after the first authenticated inbound record, keeps the wire format unchanged, and includes red-on-revert tests plus a full `cargo test --release` run with 3,510 tests passing and `go build ./...` green.

### [Event-stream sequence numbers become atomic with enqueue](https://github.com/psaab/xpf/pull/3883) — Paul Saab / xpf
A merged xpf PR fixes two Fable-review findings in cross-worker event-stream sequencing. Producers previously allocated `next_seq` before `try_send`, so concurrent workers could enqueue frames in inverted sequence order, and a full channel could burn a sequence number without a frame; the Go reader treats both as hard gaps and triggers full owner-RG resyncs plus disconnects. The patch allocates and enqueues under a producer lock, rolls back sequence numbers on full-channel drops, keeps the wire format unchanged, and reports deterministic red-on-revert tests plus 3,511 release-mode Rust tests and `go build ./...` green.

### [A feed reader hardens DNS rebinding, CSP, and SSRF edges](https://github.com/bcrisp4/bfeed/pull/51) — Ben Crisp
bfeed’s B11 security batch is explicitly tied to a “Fable audit remediation” milestone and addresses nine defense-in-depth findings around an existing SSRF guard. The fixes include Host-header validation returning 421 for cross-origin hosts, capped `Retry-After` parsing, explicit oversized-body rejection instead of silent truncation, default fetch timeouts, extra blocked network ranges, idle eviction for per-host semaphores, `noreferrer` links, CSP and related security headers, and narrower `gosec` suppressions. The PR reports unit tests for each class, `make test-race`, `make lint`, and `make sqlc-check` green, plus an end-to-end server check confirming 200 for a matching host, 421 for a foreign host, `/healthz` loopback exemption, and htmx navigation working under the CSP.

### [A game camera director ships with a Fable-caught restore bug fixed](https://github.com/EKINSOL-DEV/crewhub2/pull/13) — ekinsol / Crewhub2
Crewhub2 merged a Fable co-authored “camera director” milestone for a robot-management game: clicking rooms or HQ now frames the building, clicking a robot starts a live follow cam, Escape or the camera chip restores the previous shot, and manual drag/WASD hands control back. The PR says the final Fable whole-branch review caught a real blocker where an older chat-focus prop raced the follow snapshot, so Escape flew back to the wrong place after every robot click; the fix removed the legacy prop and added a drag dead-zone. The merge notes report 1,423 tests across 136 files green, TypeScript clean, build clean, and unchanged performance.

### [Feed audit fixes malformed RSS URLs and a dozen feed-edge cases](https://github.com/hyperlink-academy/leaflet/pull/338) — Jared Pereira / Hyperlink Academy
Leaflet used Fable 5 on an RSS, Atom, and JSON Feed audit that found a concrete interoperability bug: pretty-printed RSS placed a newline and indentation after `<link>url</link>`, and HTML-parser-based consumers treated `<link>` as void, folding the whitespace into requested URLs such as `/%0A%20%20...`. The PR minifies inter-tag whitespace outside CDATA and also fixes feed filters, invalid published dates, all-history rendering, missing RSS descriptions, XML-illegal control characters, legacy publication fallback URLs, deterministic build dates, empty canvas-post bodies, absolute image URLs, and JSON-feed caching. ### [A legal-document coverage denominator jumps from 59.6% to 89.2%](https://github.com/CodeNameHash/precedent-machine/pull/63) — Ben Goodchild / CodeNameHash
Precedent Machine’s Fable co-authored QA fix starts from a specific SEC filing failure: Kraft’s charter exhibit tail ran into an index of defined terms, by-laws, and tax opinions, but the ancillary-region detector stopped excluding at the definition appendix header. Roughly 200,000 characters re-entered the denominator, so a fully extracted filing scored only 59.6% coverage. The patch excludes the whole tail while carving the definition appendix back in, adds a missing charter-title pattern, and raises the Kraft coverage calculation to 89.2% with a targeted verification test.

### [A trading scanner recovers large-cap and ETF reversal setups](https://github.com/zmburr/backtester/pull/8) — zmburr
A Fable-authored backtester PR found that a 3DGapFade classifier had been calibrated on medium and small stocks, so flat thresholds like gap ≥4% and 9EMA ≥30% silently dropped large liquid names and ETFs before scoring. The fix derives per-cap thresholds from 36 labeled trades, passes cap through the historical backscanner and live scanner paths, and loosens the script prefilter only enough to stay below the loosest gate. Validation on the project’s reversal CSVs reports labeled recall moving from 18/36 to 32/36, real CSV trades typed in the universe scan from 3 to 10 of 23, and small/micro false positives tightening from 182 to 86 and 18 to 0.

### [Rocky 8 packaging gets an older glibc lane and executable-mode gate](https://github.com/tacitness/wmaker-ng/pull/73) — Joel Hanger / tacitness

The author reports a full local container simulation with 16 packages built, correct names, mode gate passing, and both repository trees signed.

### [A Goodix fingerprint driver stops hanging on a real Lenovo laptop](https://github.com/TheWeirdDev/libfprint/pull/5) — 3mn2 / TheWeirdDev
A libfprint PR co-authored by Fable fixes a hardware-specific enrollment and unlock hang on a Lenovo IdeaPad Flex 5 14ABR8 with a Goodix 55b4 sensor. The firmware never fires the expected finger-release event, so after the first capture the state machine stayed in `SWITCH TO FDT UP`; the patch detects release by polling frame differences against the calibration background, cancels pending polls during deactivate, and raises touch thresholds after measuring background noise at 4–25, residue at 103–108, light grazes at 145–190, and firm presses at 300–780. The report says the resulting driver was verified end-to-end with `fprintd-enroll` and `fprintd-verify`, including clean release and no command-pipeline wedge.

### [A booting NT-shaped Rust kernel appears in one Fable run](https://tolmo.com/blog/when-the-model-writes-the-kernel/) — Twinkle and Matt Suiche / Tolmo
Tolmo reports that Claude Fable 5 took an empty directory to a booting NT-shaped Rust kernel core in one contiguous 38-minute active run, touching 43 files and about 5,100 lines while using 110 tool calls. ### [A medical companion skips unknown units instead of guessing](https://github.com/PatientTrac/patienttrac-companion/pull/5) — PatientTrac
PatientTrac merged fixes from an adversarial Claude Fable 5 review of live DIL and lab-code changes. ### [A SYN-cookie secret stops leaking into a world-readable snapshot](https://github.com/psaab/xpf/pull/3914) — Paul Saab / xpf
xpf merged a Fable-review fix for a userspace dataplane snapshot that wrote `syn_cookie_master_key` into `state.json` with normal process umask permissions. The PR explains that the key validates XDP-generated SYN cookies, so a local user who could read the snapshot could forge cookies and bypass source validation during a SYN flood. The fix mirrors existing WireGuard secret handling with `skip_serializing`, audits the other snapshot key fields, regenerates the protocol fixture, and adds a red-on-revert test proving the field and key bytes no longer appear in serialized state.

### [Finance tests stop passing by asserting their own inputs](https://github.com/yeferson59/gofinance/pull/5) — yeferson59 / gofinance
A Fable co-authored gofinance PR found that many finance tests were not testing the formulas they named. Period and interest tests set non-zero period or rate inputs and then asserted the stored value back, annuity tests only checked that outputs were positive, and loose tolerances hid incorrect expectations such as treating a 10% effective annual rate compounded semiannually as a nominal-rate calculation. The merged patch rewrites the tests to force the derivation paths, documents closed-form expected values next to assertions, keeps stored-value shortcuts covered separately, and reports that production code needed no changes once the library was checked against the corrected formulas.

### [SPAKE2 hardening normalizes Ed25519 decoding and scrubs secrets](https://github.com/tv-labs/spake2/pull/1) — David Bernheisel / tv-labs
A Fable co-authored PR to tv-labs’ SPAKE2 implementation tightened several cryptographic and operational edges in one pass. The Ed25519 decoder now matches BoringSSL’s `x25519_ge_frombytes_vartime` behavior by reducing the 255-bit y value modulo p and leaving zero x coordinates reduced even when the sign bit is set; confirmation-token length mismatches now fail cleanly instead of raising through `:crypto.hash_equals/2`. The same branch redacts key material and password-derived values from inspection output, scrubs private keys and password scalars once derived, adds SRI hashes for documentation CDN assets, and includes 108 new test lines across the security cases.

### [A Strava workflow stops printing refreshed tokens to public logs](https://github.com/berensp/berensp.github.io/pull/2411) — Paul Berens
Paul Berens used Fable on a small but high-impact GitHub Actions fix for his Strava stats workflow. The patch removes the impossible secret-write step, masks both refreshed access and refresh tokens with `::add-mask::`, and adds response validation so Strava errors such as “Application Inactive” fail with a clear diagnostic instead of a JavaScript undefined-property crash.

### [A wasm-to-Go compiler stops emitting invalid amd64 extends](https://github.com/goccy/wasm2go/pull/17) — Masaaki Goshima / wasm2go
wasm2go used Fable 5 on a compiler robustness fix exposed by a cross-function inlining prototype: constant propagation left unary width conversions in place, and the amd64 emitter could turn an extended constant into an illegal instruction such as `MOVLQSX $-1, AX`. The PR folds sign-extend, zero-extend, and truncation of integer constants in ConstProp, then also makes the amd64 emitter materialize constants before extension so the invariant does not depend on earlier passes. The author reports regenerated bundles byte-identical for current consumers, plus `go test ./...` on host amd64 and `GOARCH=arm64`, `make lint`, and a new `TestConstPropFoldsWidthConversions` covering negative, `INT32_MAX`, and above-2^32 cases.

### [Yjs and Adaptify assumptions become characterization tests](https://github.com/NickDarvey/Ylmish/pull/126) — Nick Darvey
Ylmish used Fable 5 to turn design assumptions from a redesign plan into executable guardrails before the larger implementation proceeds. The PR ports the plan’s Yjs assumptions into `Y.Assumptions.fs` and adds Adaptify tests showing that IndexList structural operations emit minimal deltas while rebuilds and reorders degrade to positional rewrites, in contrast with key-stable `HashMap` behavior. Across 655 additions, the branch pins the semantics that the new design relies on so a future Yjs or Adaptify change fails CI loudly instead of silently invalidating the architecture.

### [A spec audit finds claims files the shipped schema rejects](https://github.com/jyang234/verdi-go/pull/98) — jyang234
verdi-go used Fable 5 for a Phase 3 design audit of a graph-claims tool against its consumer feature request and behavioral spec. The audit found that although FR-2 and FR-3 were satisfied and FR-1 had been hardened, the shipped strict decoder rejected spec-conformant claims files because it refused the spec’s `id` field and `fn` anchor name, producing `unknown field "id"` and exit 2 before the consumer’s 138-claim suite could run. The resulting spec splits the next work into a conformance-closure stream for `id`, `fn`, and report-line shape, and a separate `flowmap graph --mermaid --focus` stream with explicit rules for regex commas, zero matches, and boundary disclosures.

### [macOS CI caching stops using a Linux SwiftPM path](https://github.com/paulhkang94/markview/pull/36) — Paul Kang / MarkView
MarkView merged a Fable co-authored CI wall-clock cleanup after finding that macOS 15 runners were caching `~/.cache/org.swift.swiftpm`, a Linux SwiftPM path that was never populated. The fix moves SwiftPM caching to `~/Library/Caches/...`, adds Playwright and npm cache tuning, avoids duplicate guard workflow runs on PR pushes, and aligns extended-workflow cache keys with the main CI namespace. The PR estimates typical savings of 30–60 seconds and eliminates a 2m31s Playwright run on non-rendering PRs, while documenting the remaining Bundle job as the next target.

### [An optimistic-billing path stops minting affiliate overage](https://github.com/elizaOS/eliza/pull/12731) — NubsCarson / elizaOS
elizaOS merged a Fable-authored fix for a residual billing bug in `/v1/embeddings` when optimistic billing and affiliate markup were both enabled. The previous synchronous path reserved base cost plus markup, but the DB-ledger and KV optimistic fast paths admitted on base cost only, allowing an attacker-set affiliate markup of up to 1000% to settle as redeemable earnings without matching balance headroom. The patch routes requests with `X-Affiliate-Code` through the synchronous reserve path, and the PR reports mutation-verified tests where reverting the gate or dropping `affiliateCode` from reserve makes two tests fail, with all four embeddings suites at 29 passing tests plus biome and typecheck clean.

### [Clojure interpreter promotion stops corrupting special forms](https://github.com/csm/clojurust/pull/260) — Casey Marshall
clojurust found a promotion bug where code worked in the tree-walker and then broke once a function crossed the background IR-lowering threshold. The Fable-authored PR fixes four concrete classes: `(.method ...)` interop no longer becomes a missing `.method` global, slash-named builtins such as `Math/abs` retry the joined symbol, `(var f)` lowers like `#'f`, and `with-out-str` captures output in the IR interpreter instead of calling a nil stub. Forms with no IR equivalent, including `defprotocol`, `extend-type`, `defrecord`, `deftype`, and `reify`, are now rejected by lowering so they stay interpreted rather than silently corrupting after promotion.

### [Kafka catches truncated list entries instead of zero-padding them](https://github.com/apache/kafka/pull/22755) — Sepuri Sai Krishna / Apache Kafka
A Kafka PR co-authored with Claude Fable 5 fixes a narrow deserialization bug in `ListDeserializer`. The old code treated only `-1` from `DataInputStream.read(byte[])` as truncation, so a payload declaring a 10-byte entry but providing only 5 bytes could pass the size check, get zero-padded, and deserialize as corrupted data instead of throwing `SerializationException`. The patch switches to `readFully`, maps `EOFException` to Kafka’s existing premature-end error, and adds a regression test that fails without the fix while the full `ListDeserializerTest`, checkstyle, and spotless pass locally.

### [Kafka stops inventing leader epoch zero when the cache cannot answer](https://github.com/apache/kafka/pull/22756) — Sepuri Sai Krishna / Apache Kafka
A second Kafka PR co-authored with Claude Fable 5 fixes an inconsistency between `LocalLeaderEndPoint` and the remote ListOffsets path. When the local leader epoch cache could not resolve an offset, the local path fabricated epoch 0, while the remote path serialized `NO_LEADER_EPOCH` as -1; downstream tiered-storage code treated the fake zero as a meaningful first epoch. The patch returns `UNDEFINED_EPOCH` for all four unresolved local-offset methods and replaces self-referential tests with concrete cases that fail on the old behavior, with `LocalLeaderEndPointTest` and `ReplicaAlterLogDirsThreadTest` passing locally.

### [A proxy turns Claude Code context into images to cut tokens](https://github.com/teamchong/pxpipe) — teamchong
pxpipe is a local proxy that rewrites Claude Code's bulky request context — system prompt, tool docs, older history, code, JSON, and tool output — into dense PNG pages before the request leaves the machine. The README shows Fable 5 reading a rendered page containing about 48,000 characters for roughly 2,700 image tokens instead of about 25,000 text tokens, then completing a demo that counts an exact token across 39 imaged filler files, solves a ledger task, and ends at $6.06 versus $42.21 for the text-only run. The project also documents the failure mode: exact 12-character hex strings in dense images were read 13/15 times by Fable 5 and 0/15 times by Opus, with misses described as silent confabulations rather than clean errors.

### [Hosted sandbox quotas stop using a zero live counter](https://github.com/mitos-run/mitos/pull/689) — Jannes Stubbemann / Mitos
Mitos used Fable 5 on hosted Firecracker microVM quota enforcement after finding that the gateway's live-usage source was a zero stub and console billing suspensions were computed but dropped. The PR adds a Kubernetes-backed `LiveCounter` that counts non-terminal `Sandbox` replicas, fails closed on list errors, runs a startup self-check for RBAC and scheme problems, and wires hard-spend-cap or dunning suspensions into the shared Postgres table the gateway reads. The 29-file branch also updates the threat model and docs to say exactly which caps are enforced and which remain deferred, with five Fable co-authored commits in the reviewed slice.

### [A WebGL VJ tool syncs Droste visuals to beats and MIDI](https://github.com/nickybu/dj-utils/pull/1) — nickybu
DROSTE is a Fable 5 co-authored WebGL2 visual-performance tool built around an Escher-style infinite-zoom renderer. The 1,700-line PR adds BPM input, tap tempo, resync, microphone beat detection with onset-based phase pull and auto-BPM estimation, MIDI-learn on every parameter, persisted presets, JSON export/import, four pattern styles, kaleidoscope fold, domain warp, feedback trails, strobe, and a de Smit-Lenstra “Print Gallery” conformal-map preset with branch-cut crossfade. It is still an open PR, but the implementation is concrete enough to inspect as a complete browser artifact rather than a plan.

### [A portfolio dashboard clips intraday charts to market open](https://github.com/BKodeerts/portfolio-tracker/pull/22) — BKodeerts
portfolio-tracker merged a Fable 5 co-authored frontend foundation pass across 18 files, replacing much of the dashboard surface with shared design tokens, `IntradaySparkline`, `PeriodPills`, SVG period charts, activity lists, and allocation bars. ### [KaTeX output stops becoming Markdown strikethrough](https://github.com/medewitt/ideeep/pull/12) — Matthew DeWitt
ideeep merged a Fable 5 co-authored fix for a rendering bug where KaTeX's ASCII tildes from `\tilde` accents were handed to `pulldown-cmark` with GFM strikethrough enabled. Markdown parsing paired those tildes into `<del>` runs inside KaTeX spans, corrupted the DOM, and stopped the metapopulation asynchrony page at its ANOVA variance block. The patch renders math to HTML first, replaces each math span with an inert Private Use Area placeholder during Markdown parsing, and restores the KaTeX HTML afterward so tilde, asterisk, underscore, and similar characters cannot be reinterpreted as Markdown syntax.

### [Power-grid diagrams get faster without changing reference output](https://github.com/gautierbureau/powsybl-diagram/pull/1) — gautierbureau
powsybl-diagram has a Fable co-authored performance PR that works through hot loops in force layout, network-area diagrams, and single-line diagrams. It replaces stream pipelines and repeated `Vector2D` allocations in O(n²) force calculations, avoids repeated `degreeOf()` and `List.indexOf()` lookups, buckets graph edges in one O(E) pass, memoizes expensive IDs and style lookups, and swaps `String.format` coordinates for a BigDecimal-based formatter measured about 2.5x faster. The PR says all reference SVG and JSON tests pass unchanged, with floating-point operation order preserved so layouts and outputs stay byte-identical.

### [A React Native tooling library cuts build time from 53 seconds to 2](https://github.com/callstack/agent-device/pull/1087) — thymikee / Callstack
Callstack's `agent-device` moved its library build from Rspack-based rslib to tsdown and Rolldown in a Fable co-authored PR. The reported build-time result is roughly 53 seconds down to 2 seconds, with the npm tarball 3.0 kB smaller and CLI `--version` startup about 3 ms faster, while the remaining +0.6% gzip size is attributed to OXC versus SWC minification. The write-up also records rejected chunk-merging experiments, including a shared chunk that added about 140 ms to `--help` startup, and keeps declaration bundling plus package-entry contracts unchanged.

### [A support token-reset tool learns how to revive manual subscriptions](https://github.com/superwizor/ai/pull/55) — Piotr Dąbrowski / Superwizor
Superwizor found a billing edge case in production-style testing: its Polish "reset tokens" support tool failed with `SUBSCRIPTION_INACTIVE` for every non-Stripe organization after the first billing period, because MANUAL subscriptions were canceled at period end and no usage counter existed. The Fable co-authored fix reactivates only MANUAL subscriptions in place, creates the org-level counter for the fresh period, records `subscription_reactivated` in the audit row, and leaves Stripe subscriptions under Stripe's source of truth. The PR says the failure was live-tested on a specific org and that billing service build, vet, and tests are green.

### [A Lightning node fork adds default-off circular self-payments](https://github.com/lamtuanvu/ldk-node/pull/5) — tonible14012002
A Fable co-authored slice of an `ldk-node` fork adds a `cycles` feature for manual-route circular self-payments, the primitive needed by a cooperative cycle-balance engine. The new `Node::send_along_route` sends along a caller-supplied route without pathfinding, registers the hash with LDK's stateless inbound-payment verifier so the looped HTLC is receivable, and stores a new `PaymentKind::Rebalance` record carrying the hash and preimage. The feature is default-off, avoids a Lightning crate version bump and wallet or monitor format changes, and the event handler only reveals the preimage for at least the recorded loop amount.

### [Protein ribbon playback gets a measured 2.43x renderer speedup](https://github.com/hodakamori/megane/pull/556) — hodakamori
