### [A stack-slot audit finds silent arm64 memory corruption](https://github.com/marcelocantos/csp/pull/88) — Marcelo Cantos
csp is remediating a Fable 5 audit finding where `spawn()` chose a Small stack slot from checkpoint-sampled high-water data instead of a sound exact analyzer bound. On arm64, a mis-sized process could run past the 4 KB software guard into a neighboring slot without a SIGSEGV, silently corrupting it. The fix drops the profile-to-Small path, adds a differential `stack_slot_sizing` test that fails on unfixed master and passes after the change, and reports the full `ANALYSE=1` suite green at 757/757 tests with 26,491 assertions.

### [Water-reflection edges switch from cell staircases to contours](https://github.com/bwdrebing/Eden/pull/5) — bwdrebing
Eden merged a compact Fable 5 co-authored rendering fix for jagged 2D panorama reflections. The old path rebuilt diagonal or curved painted regions as staircase pieces from elevation rows and azimuth column swaths, producing shredded slivers and clip-path hairlines; the new path samples a signed-distance field through the reflected-direction fields, contours it at zero, and stacks color regions as nested upper sets so smoothing cannot open background gaps. The PR also records practical rendering fixes discovered along the way: one-cell padding, pushing contours past the projected water outline, clipping to the trapezoid, and forcing an isolated buffer so antialiasing happens once against the composite.

### [A compiler fix closes regex, checker, and LSP holes](https://github.com/accuser/bynk/pull/525) — Matthew Gibbons
A Fable 5 co-authored Bynk compiler PR starts with a concrete input-validation bypass: generated `Matches("ab|cd")` refinements became `/^ab|cd$/`, so strings like `abZZZ` and `ZZZcd` passed checks guarding HTTP params and bodies. The same branch adds diagnostics for unknown names, unknown calls, arity mismatches, and agent-handler argument mismatches that previously passed through handler bodies, rejects indirect recursive record cycles that could overflow zero-value emission, makes type-relation arms exhaustive, and fixes LSP cursor math that treated UTF-16 positions as bytes. The PR adds negative and positive compiler fixtures plus a `tsc`/Node behavior test for the regex bypass.

### [Graph neural-network hot paths cut JAX warmup time](https://github.com/gautierbureau/energnn/pull/1) — Gautier Bureau
An Energnn PR co-authored by Claude Fable 5 attacks several measured JAX and graph-processing bottlenecks rather than changing model behavior. It builds and pads LinearSystem graphs on the NumPy side before transferring one collated batch to JAX, replaces a Python-unrolled recurrent message-passing loop with `jax.lax.scan`, removes unconditional per-stage `block_until_ready` synchronizations, and avoids repeated concatenation, stacking, and percentile work in graph statistics. The CPU quick-start numbers in the PR show batch generation dropping from 413ms to 7ms, training warmup from 19.2s to 6.0s, steady-state training from 213ms to 107ms per step, and the test suite from 63s to 44s.

### [Surface Evolver benchmark puts Fable first on custom physics files](https://x.com/Deep_Burner/status/2073469052089946277) — Deep_Burner
Deep_Burner added `claude-fable-5 (high)` to a Surface Evolver benchmark that asks models to write valid custom datafiles for liquid-surface simulations. The published chart shows Fable passing 14 of 16 tasks with a 0.95 mean score, ahead of GPT-5.5 high at 12 of 16 and 0.88. It also used 933k total tokens, about 58k per run, versus GPT-5.5 high at 2.0M total tokens and 127k per run, though the Fable run still cost more at $19.44.

### [Post-quantum Kaspa covenants deployed with mainnet proofs](https://x.com/mrZeku2000x/status/2073496612593143958) — mrZeku2000x
mrZeku2000x reports using Fable 5 to read Kaspa/Toccata GitHub Markdown, generate XMSS covenant scripts, compile them, and deploy them on Kaspa mainnet. The resulting open-source `kaspa-xmss-covenants` repo describes hash-based XMSS-SHA2_10_192 authentication using native Kaspa P2SH covenants rather than elliptic-curve signatures, with transaction IDs for deployed-and-spent claims in `docs/MAINNET_PROOFS.md`. The README is also explicit about remaining limits, including off-chain leaf-reuse tracking and a QR hardware-signer workflow that is still only a design spec.

### [A crypto crate replaces security theater with real hybrid primitives](https://github.com/redasgard/quantum-shield/pull/1) — ilyk / redasgard
quantum-shield used Fable 5 first to delete a non-compiling `security.rs` module whose sleep jitter, XOR blinding, entropy counter, and hard-coded audit trail added latency without protection, then to rewrite the crate around X25519 plus ML-KEM-1024 hybrid KEM and Ed25519 plus ML-DSA-87 signatures. The PR touches 622 files with about 8,188 additions and 8,084 deletions, adds a Linux and Apple Silicon CI matrix, MSRV and `no_std` checks, cargo-deny, and production-readiness docs. All listed checks are green on the open PR, including duplicated Ubuntu/macOS test runs, MSRV 1.85, thumbv7em `no_std`, cargo-deny, docs, and version consistency.

### [An API-to-MCP generator adds catalogs, OAuth refresh, Python output, and HTTP serving](https://github.com/krishgok/mcp-api-translator/pull/9) — krishgok
mcp-api-translator has a Fable 5 co-authored roadmap branch that starts with a machine-readable `tool-catalog.json` for generated MCP servers, then layers in OAuth2 refresh-token support, per-API base URL and auth namespacing, a FastMCP-flavored Python output target, and Dockerized HTTP serving. The catalog deliberately records cheap discovery fields — name, summary, tags, method, path, and source — so a client-side tool-search layer can rank tools without loading full schemas or request plans. The open PR spans 28 files and reports green build, generated-output, and DCO checks.

### [Long-session exports stop corrupting after 255 turns](https://github.com/rekal-dev/rekal-cli/pull/5) — rekal-dev
A merged Fable 5-authored Rekal CLI PR fixes silent corruption in the tool’s Git-backed session wire format. The old v1 frames stored turn, tool-call, checkpoint, and dictionary counts in one-byte or u16 fields, so a 300-turn session could decode as 44 turns and large agent teams could wrap the email namespace; the new v2 frames and dictionary use bounded varints while keeping small v1 frames readable by older binaries. The same branch carries harness metadata through sync, adds a `--re-export` repair path for already-corrupt derived branches, moves version notices off JSON stdout, fixes UTF-8 snippet boundaries and no-space panics, and merged with CI, lint, and license checks green.

### [Quantum gate caches stop snapping angles to the wrong matrices](https://github.com/glanzz/simq/pull/44) — Bhargav C N / simq
A Fable 5 co-authored simq PR traces a numerical bug through several layers of a Rust quantum-simulation stack: cached RX/RZ and generated rotation lookups were returning the nearest grid matrix for generic angles, with errors up to about 3.3e-3 per gate and finite-difference gradients collapsing to zero. The fix makes caches exact-match-only unless an explicitly approximate path is requested, makes Clifford+T decomposition reject arbitrary angles instead of silently rounding by as much as π/8, enforces the advertised rotation-table tolerance, and adds a 20,000-point dispatch sweep plus VQE gradient regressions. The open PR reports macOS tests, code coverage, and security audit checks green.

### [JSON:API relationships land with SQL-windowed batch tests](https://github.com/haddowg/json-api-laravel/pull/5) — Greg Haddow
Greg Haddow merged a large Fable-assisted phase of json-api-laravel that adds relationship reads, mutations, pivot fields, existence filters, and the Relationship Queries profile. The implementation deliberately pushes windowed relationship batches into SQL with `ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY parent ...)`, while an in-memory witness must produce byte-identical tied-key pages; along the way review caught real defects including pivot IDs clobbering related IDs, BelongsTo linkage N+1 queries, poisoned Eloquent attribute snapshots, page leakage onto parent models, and wrong JSON pointer locations. The PR adds more than 13,000 lines and merged with a 12-combination PHP/Laravel matrix, static analysis, and coding-standards checks green; the author also reports 725 local tests and 6,358 assertions.

### [JAX compilation cache helper documents where caching stops](https://github.com/gautierbureau/energnn/pull/5) — Gautier Bureau
A follow-up Fable 5 PR to Energnn adds `enable_persistent_compilation_cache()`, a one-call wrapper around JAX’s on-disk compilation cache so XLA executables can survive fresh Python processes. The useful part is the boundary condition: the PR verifies across two fresh processes that backward executables and evaluation forwards cache-hit, while training-mode forwards that contain `io_callback` from `TDigestNormalizer` cannot be persisted and are documented as such. The quick-start Small model’s second-process first training step drops from 3.4s to 2.5s rather than pretending to remove all warmup cost, and the author reports the full 200-test suite passing.

### [Org-mode date ranges become real multi-day events](https://github.com/ikigai-rs/ikigai-org/pull/5) — Brian Sletten
A merged Claude Fable 5 co-authored ikigai-org PR fixes how the calendar importer reads Org-mode `<start>--<end>` ranges. Previously the parser split a four-day stay into unrelated single-day stamps, so it appeared only on the first day and the end day; the new path merges the pair into one event carrying the range end, with all-day ranges using exclusive `dtend`, timed ranges staying continuous, repeaters keeping their duration, and ranges crossing the window start still included. The patch changes three files, adds focused coverage, and passed the project CI check.

## 2026-07-05

### [A local-agent benchmark harness beats chatbot-style testing](https://x.com/Topaz750/status/2073331746217538012) — Cyril / Topaz750
Cyril used Fable 5 for a 35-minute operator test: optimize a Rapid-MLX local Qwen3.6-35B MoE setup on a Mac Mini M4 Pro for agent reliability rather than chat throughput. The model built a standard-library Python benchmark harness, restarted the server across eight configurations, measured cold and warm behavior, and scored tool-call correctness. The selected setup used k8v4 KV cache, 4096 prefill, a single concurrent sequence, opt-in thinking, and a capped disk KV cache, reaching about 80 tokens per second, 0.22s warm TTFT, and 11/11 tool-call suite success while also finding that native int4/chunked prefill, concurrency, and always-on thinking each hurt real agent behavior.

### [Two SDRs keep their capture windows within 200 ns](https://github.com/lgarrido581/plutoplus-gps-timing/pull/5) — Crusader8494 / plutoplus-gps-timing
A merged Fable co-authored PR fixes a timing assumption in a Pluto+ GPS capture stack: ADI's `axi_tdd` only syncs once at enable, so an apparently PPS-wired one-second frame still free-ran and accumulated millisecond drift. The patch gates RX DMA from a `pps_counter` frame that reloads on every PPS edge, keeps streaming RX on the old path through an OR gate, and documents the required bitstream change. After building the bitstream and flashing two radios, the author reports cross-radio capture-window deltas dropping from accumulating milliseconds to a bounded 0–200 ns, with `method=tdd_pps_latch` and `latch_rms=16 ns` on every capture.

### [A GraphRAG semantic-search layer refuses uncited hits](https://github.com/CLYEH/graphRAG/pull/31) — CLYEH / graphRAG
graphRAG has an open Fable 5 co-authored PR adding the project's first semantic retrieval modality over Qdrant and Postgres. The implementation embeds a query with the same abstraction used at indexing time, runs build-scoped kNN, enriches chunk and entity hits into the frozen response schema, and drops results that cannot cite a source instead of emitting uncited answers or crashing. The branch adds unit, contract, and live PG+Qdrant integration tests for nearest cited results and active-build isolation, with a follow-up commit specifically handling corrupt non-UUID payload IDs as partial results.

### [A mortgage lock-in paper changes its own headline numbers](https://github.com/eugeneoCMU/Lock-in-Effect/pull/1) — Eugene O / Lock-in-Effect
A merged Fable co-authored robustness pass for a mortgage lock-in study froze a pre-fix baseline, then applied four attributable fixes to the empirical and simulation pipelines. The most consequential one found that the Path B elasticity coefficient was being applied to a decimal rate gap rather than per 100 basis points, moving the hazard estimate from $747.3B to $818.5B with an $810B–$828B band. A 15-year MBS fold-in moved the ABM trapped estimate from $101.2B to $91.0B, while a new Freddie cross-design test recovered 59.3% under recalibration and explicitly weakened an earlier paradigm claim rather than confirming it. The PR merged with seven regression tests plus exact baseline/no-regression checks for 30-year-only and synthetic ABM modes.

### [A tool-selection funnel uses the LLM only after deterministic narrowing](https://github.com/ikigai-rs/ikigai-cli/pull/120) — Brian Sletten / ikigai-cli
ikigai-cli has an open Claude Fable 5 co-authored PR for `urn:agent:select`, a graph-shaped action-selection resource. The code first narrows authorized actions deterministically by capability, verb, wanted resource, and type; it calls the LLM only when several authorized actions survive and a goal is present, and inference failures degrade to a ranked candidate list rather than an error. The PR records a live end-to-end check where “put a dentist appointment on my calendar” selected `calendar:action:sink` with rationale, plus an attenuation test showing that a freebusy capability cannot surface write actions.

### [An audit-to-outreach backend gets reviewable drafts and webhook state transitions](https://github.com/Abuzar0021/omnistacks-ai-engine/pull/5) — Abuzar0021 / omnistacks-ai-engine
omnistacks-ai-engine has an open Claude-authored milestone PR that turns completed business audits into reviewable outreach drafts and then sent emails. The branch adds an `EmailDraft` table and status lifecycle, constrains the model to generating only subject, opener, and cited fact while the CTA and signature come from code, and keeps sending behind an explicit `POST /api/email-drafts/:id/send` that triggers n8n separately from drafting. ### [A sidecar install crash-loop is found in a live external-app test](https://github.com/KazukiKandaKK/webgrapgh/pull/35) — KazukiKandaKK / webgrapgh
webgrapgh’s Fable co-authored sidecar fix comes from exercising the deployment against an external heavy-load app, not from a synthetic unit failure. The sidecar compose file used `SEED_POINTS_PER_METRIC=0` to mean “no demo data,” but the backend passed zero into a bulk seeder that rejects non-positive values, crash-looping every fresh install. The one-file fix treats zero as seeding disabled, and the PR reports `go build/vet/test ./...` plus a live sidecar run where the backend reached `listening`, the collector discovered the external app’s containers, and `/api/containers/history` returned real CPU and memory series.

### [Out-of-order database commits stop losing channel messages](https://github.com/h11t-labs/firm/pull/5) — h11t-labs
Firm merged a Fable-linked channel-delivery fix for a real Postgres/MySQL race: autoincrement ids are assigned at insert time but become visible at commit time, so a listener that advanced a max-id cursor could permanently skip a lower-id message that committed late. The new listener re-scans above a floor, de-duplicates dispatched ids, and only advances past rows older than a documented `commit_grace` window. Tests include the exact two-connection interleaving that lost messages before, with the SQLite path skipped because its single writer cannot reproduce the race.

Later commits in the same PR replace a polling receive handoff with `sem_clockwait`, fix an enqueue ordering race that could expose partially written queue slots, and move stalled streamer pipe writes off the router main loop into a bounded writer thread.

### [AsyncIterator hot paths get measured 16–36% wins](https://github.com/jeswr/AsyncIterator/pull/5) — Ruben Taelman / AsyncIterator

### [A copy-paste option bug toggled remote lookups](https://github.com/jeswr/Components.js/pull/5) — Jesse Wright / Components.js
Jesse Wright staged a Fable-generated Components.js fix for a one-line copy-paste bug with outsized behavior. `ComponentsManagerBuilder` assigned `Boolean(options.typeChecking)` to `this.remoteContextLookups` whenever `remoteContextLookups` was defined, so `remoteContextLookups: true` with `typeChecking: false` silently disabled remote lookup, while `remoteContextLookups: false` with default type checking silently enabled the network-access path. The PR changes the assignment and adds a regression test pinning the two options as independent, with the author noting it was generated by Claude Fable 5 for review before upstreaming and the full suite still at 100% coverage.

### [A circuit-simulator cross-check traces a 50 mV solver offset](https://github.com/NyanCAD/Cadnip.jl/pull/208) — Pepijn de Vos / Cadnip.jl
Cadnip has an open Fable-authored fix for a roughly 1e-4 relative-L2 mismatch against VACASK on a diode-voltage-multiplier benchmark. The PR traces the error to DC Newton termination on an absolute residual: weakly conducting floating diode-chain nodes could stop about 50 mV below the driven 50 V level, while VACASK and ngspice landed at 50.000000 V and 50.000058 V. A follow-up Fable commit found a second source of bias, where anchoring Verilog-A internal nodes to ground leaked about 50 pA per node; the branch adds a voltage-update Newton polish, anchors internal gmin to the first terminal instead, and pins the case with a floating-chain regression test.

### [Hugo .Render learns nested layout lookup](https://github.com/gohugoio/hugo/pull/15091) — Bjørn Erik Pedersen / Hugo

### [Graph node clicks stop blanking the whole app](https://github.com/samibel/graphi/pull/40) — samibel / Graphi
Graphi used Fable on a UI failure that came from a specific Sigma v3 mismatch: node clicks in compare-off mode converted citation edges to a `dashed` type even though only `line` and `arrow` edge programs were registered, throwing the renderer and unmounting the app to a white screen. The fix keeps citation edges as styled lines, adds a graph error boundary, makes node positions deterministic instead of `Math.random()` on every SSE refresh, labels nodes and edge kinds, and repairs edge-click lookup keys. The PR reports an embedded-UI Playwright run covering load, click, highlight rendering, and no page errors.

Its benchmarked allocation pass reports BFS path memory down 18% and time down 25%, Dijkstra corner-to-corner allocations down 36%, and connected-components allocations down 25%.

### [Mac brightness sliders resync with real hardware state](https://github.com/VenkateshDas/pulse/pull/43) — Venkatesh Das / Pulse
Pulse used Fable on two concrete macOS brightness bugs: hardware changes from media keys, Control Center, or auto-brightness did not flow back into the app’s slider state, and writing the same value through both user-scale and linear DisplayServices APIs could turn a requested 0.78 into a measured 0.91 user brightness. The fix registers per-display brightness-change notifications, initializes the observer at launch, drops echoes from Pulse’s own writes with a half-second guard, and stops calling `SetLinearBrightness` except at the scale’s shared endpoint. The PR is only 74 additions across four files, but the body explains the Swift 6 isolation constraint and the user-visible drift it repairs.

### [Taylor models land with thesis examples as regression tests](https://github.com/andreapasquale94/tax/pull/31) — Andrea Pasquale / tax
A Claude Fable 5-authored tax PR adds a header-only C++ implementation of Makino-style Taylor models for rigorous remainder bounds, then extends it with a quadratic range bounder, ODE-integration primitives, and Eigen compatibility. The branch is explicit about the math it is pinning: outward-rounded interval arithmetic, domain-checked intrinsics, polynomial-excess folding into remainders, Picard-step helpers, and abstract constants so Eigen’s generated zero and one literals can safely adopt a model domain. The tests include interval and intrinsic containment sweeps plus thesis worked examples from sections 4.15/4.16, Tables 4.2 and 4.3, enclosure functions, a verified double integral, a harmonic-oscillator integration check, and Eigen matrix products.

### [CJK transcript rows stop hard-wrapping at column zero](https://github.com/DylanDDeng/bubble/pull/54) — DylanDDeng / bubble
Bubble has an open Fable-authored terminal-rendering fix for a narrow but user-visible wrapping bug. Transcript rows reserved two columns of horizontal padding, but the text wrapper only subtracted the timeline gutter, so dense CJK text could be handed a budget two cells wider than the real row and force the terminal to wrap the last glyph onto a stray line at column zero. The patch names the padding constant next to the Ink `paddingX` prop and adds an end-to-end regression test that renders CJK list items and paragraphs across a width sweep while asserting every physical row fits the terminal.

### [A memory benchmark swings from 17% to 73% with scaffolding](https://x.com/ST4RHaze/status/2073875623995683060) — StarHaze

### [A disk scanner stops counting firmlinked data twice](https://github.com/VenkateshDas/pulse/pull/45) — Venkatesh Das / Pulse
Pulse has a new Fable co-authored storage fix for a macOS-specific accounting bug. Her main lesson was to ask Fable to build procedures that lower-tier models could run later — slide-generation scaffolding, smartwatch health-data analysis and notification flows, and production manuals — rather than one-off outputs that would vanish with access to the model.

### [MCP file-editing tools are jailed behind realpath allowlists](https://github.com/cobiadigital/mcp-for-ssh-control/pull/5) — cobiadigital
A merged Fable 5 co-authored PR to `mcp-for-ssh-control` adds six new MCP tools — directory listing, file read/write/edit, script checking, and script execution — while keeping them disabled unless `ALLOWED_PATHS` is configured. Every requested path is resolved with `realpath` before use so `..` segments and symlinks cannot escape the allowed roots, and `run_script` only dispatches files inside those roots through a fixed interpreter set rather than arbitrary binaries. The patch spans the internal Node service, worker interface, README, and smoke tests that now include path-escape checks.

### [A transient roster refetch stops collapsing a money app nav bar](https://github.com/ecuaryan/bucket-my-money/pull/266) — ecuaryan / bucket-my-money

That made `childCount` hit zero, dropped the Kids/Give tab, moved Buckets to a different nav position, and then snapped back when the next refetch succeeded. The fix retries the unguarded auth-lock query, keeps the last good roster on failed refetches, broadens the shell freeze around absent member state, and adds a provider-level regression test that failed against the old code.

### [An Apple II emulator stops running twenty-five percent fast](https://github.com/st3fan/ewm/pull/206) — Stefan Arentz / ewm

### [A game-theory solver stops returning the feasible hull too early](https://github.com/QuantEcon/QuantEcon.py/pull/848) — Daisuke Oyama / QuantEcon.py
QuantEcon.py has a Fable 5 co-authored fix for a subtle Abreu–Sannikov repeated-game bug in `RepeatedGame.equilibrium_payoffs`. With the default zero threat-point initialization, the algorithm could decide it had converged before threat points were updated, returning the feasible payoff hull for a Prisoner’s Dilemma where the correct equilibrium set has vertices `[[3, 3], [9.75, 3], [9, 9], [3, 9.75]]`. The patch initializes from player-wise minimum payoffs, moves threat-point updates before convergence, raises a clearer error for empty candidate sets, and adds regression tests cross-checked against GameTheory.jl and a 256-bit BigFloat reference computation.

It also enables Allure `@Step` output through an AspectJ Surefire agent, adds compiler parameter metadata for clearer step placeholders, and documents layer rules and anti-patterns in `CLAUDE.MD` and the README.

### [MusicXML uploads learn to unwrap compressed .mxl archives](https://github.com/gionnibgud/feedBack-plugin-musicxml-import/pull/1) — gionnibgud / feedBack-plugin-musicxml-import
feedBack-plugin-musicxml-import has an open Fable 5 co-authored PR adding compressed MusicXML support to a plugin that previously only handled plain XML uploads. The parser detects zip magic bytes rather than trusting extensions, resolves the primary rootfile through `META-INF/container.xml`, skips alternate renditions such as embedded PDFs, falls back for malformed archives, and rejects traversal paths. The PR adds tests for the unwrap logic, reports `pytest tests/` at 37/37 passing, and says a real MuseScore-exported `.mxl` parsed identically to its decompressed XML before being packed into a `.feedpak` and validated by the core reader.

### [OpenClaw closes stale SQLite handles and catches an exit-listener crash before merge](https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/100827) — Alex Knight / OpenClaw
OpenClaw has an open PR marked as assisted by Claude Fable 5, with an independent GPT-5.5 review pass, for a lifecycle bug in three process-global SQLite handle caches. CLI one-shots and ACP bridge processes could exit with open `DatabaseSync` handles, skipping the final WAL checkpoint and leaving stale `-wal` and `-shm` files for the next opener; the new shared exit-close hook registers and unregisters with the cache lifecycle. While wiring it, an eight-angle adversarial finder pass surfaced a debug-proxy path where an exit listener could fetch a cached store bound to a closed handle and crash with `ERR_INVALID_STATE`, now covered by rebind tests alongside state and agent database close tests.

### [A production CORS hardening patch stopped same-origin GETs](https://github.com/Will-Massey/engage-from-capstone/pull/5) — Will Massey / engage-from-capstone
A small Fable co-authored engage-from-capstone PR is useful because the failure is precisely described. A P1 hardening change rejected requests without an `Origin` header, but browsers omit that header on same-origin GETs; behind the project’s proxy, every production GET API call returned 500 while CI missed it because development mode bypassed the gate. The fix treats originless requests as non-CORS requests and reports a production-mode check where originless `/ping` returned 200, `/api/auth/me` returned 401, and an evil Origin was still blocked.

### [Font-label validation stops losing false negatives](https://github.com/ProductPope/fontsentry/pull/27) — ProductPope / fontsentry
fontsentry’s open Fable co-authored PR fixes a validation bug that let labels silently disappear into the “not detected” bucket. The old matching stripped and lowercased text only, so variants such as `Open Sans` versus `OpenSans-Regular` could leave the agreement denominator and escape the false-negative gate. The patch folds weight and style variants through the pipeline’s own `group_key`, strips PDF subset prefixes, tolerates scheme and `www.` differences in domains, reports no-scan labels separately, and updates validation docs and tests.

### [Fable 5 as an agent CEO](https://phasetransitionsai.substack.com/p/fable-5-agent-ceo) — Graham Rowe
Graham Rowe describes using Fable 5 in Claude Code less as a chatbot and more as a manager for other agents. His setup relies on reusable skills, locked goals with pass/fail criteria, and workflows that split jobs across teams of cheaper and smarter agents. One concrete example is a voiceover screencast skill: the agent opens software, clicks through a user journey, narrates what it sees, and returns a recording that Rowe can hand to another model for friction analysis.

### [Early-access tests across vision, design, and subagents](https://www.chatprd.ai/how-i-ai/claude-fable-5-review) — Claire Vo
Claire Vo tested Fable 5 across coding, writing, design, vision, and multi-agent workflows. The strongest result was document and vision work: for handwriting-practice PDFs, she found the Fable/Mythos output clearer and better spaced than the Opus 4.8 version. Her negatives were specific too: product-spec prose became hard to parse, one-shot design for a skills registry was poor, MVP execution was overly narrow, and some subagents stalled after about three hours when she left the run unattended.

### [A file-exchange vision client lets agents inspect renders without API credentials](https://github.com/jop3/game-builder/pull/5) — jop3 / game-builder

### [A rollout regrade finds poisoned zero rewards in verifier failures](https://github.com/fleet-ai/OpenEnv/pull/21) — sumi-fleet-hub / Fleet AI
Fleet AI's OpenEnv PR is a compact but useful Fable co-authored failure analysis. A regrade census of 30 zero-reward rollouts, each regraded twice through the production verifier, found that 23% were verifier-execution failures being scored as 0.0, including one stable `[1.0, 1.0]` full pass. The author estimates that at a 28% zero rate this corrupted about 6.5% of rollout labels and roughly 42% of GRPO groups of eight; the patch broadens retry handling from a few proxy errors to any unsuccessful verifier response, with exclusion semantics left for a follow-up reward-contract change.

### [Two cell-tracking workers link segmented polygons into lineages](https://github.com/arjunrajlaboratory/ImageAnalysisProject/pull/150) — arjunrajlab / ImageAnalysisProject
ImageAnalysisProject has an open Fable 5 co-authored PR adding two biology image-analysis workers that link existing tagged polygon segmentations across time into parent-child lineage tracks. The Trackastra worker rasterizes polygons, loads channel intensities, runs the transformer tracker with GPU or CPU fallback, and maps the track graph back to annotations; the Ultrack worker builds label stacks, runs the global-optimization tracker with CBC, maps tracks by nearest-mask centroid, and derives division links from parent track IDs. The branch adds entrypoints, Dockerfiles, environments, docs, registry wiring, and 20 tests covering rasterization, graph-to-connection mapping, divisions, and mocked end-to-end compute.

### [A fitness MCP server gets real-account read tools and resources](https://github.com/gCuadros/hevy-mcp/pull/5) — Gonzalo Cuadros / hevy-mcp
hevy-mcp merged a read-tool slice that was tested against a real Hevy account rather than only mocked fixtures. The PR adds workout and routine lookup tools, exercise search, exercise-history disambiguation that returns candidates instead of guessing, and five `hevy://` resources for profile, routines, exercises, stats, and recent workouts. One concrete API discovery shaped the design: Hevy has no `/user` or `/profile` endpoint, verified live as a 404, so the profile resource became a cache-status summary; end-to-end stdio JSON-RPC checks covered sync, filtered workouts, ambiguous and resolved exercise history, routines, and stats resources.

### [A local World Cup game replaces an external link and removes injected tracking code](https://github.com/thinkhiphop12-pixel/New/pull/39) — thinkhiphop12-pixel / New

## 2026-07-07

### [Corrector deltas get carried into climate-model diagnostics](https://github.com/ai2cm/ace/pull/1335) — Jeremy Duncan / ACE
ACE has an open Fable 5 co-authored PR for a climate-model inference gap: correctors declare per-step deltas, but those effects were discarded at the `Stepper.predict` boundary, leaving no output that showed how much a forecast leaned on correction. The branch adds a `StepDiagnostics` carrier, masks deltas with the same NaN-fill output masker as predictions, writes an opt-in `autoregressive_step_diagnostics.nc` file, and deliberately leaves coupled runs for a follow-up. The PR changes 16 files with 938 additions, adds tests across batch carriage, step output, masking, and writer builders, and records review-driven reversals such as rejecting silent time-axis slicing that would misalign diagnostics.

### [Envelope-encrypted secrets land with leak-path fixes before review](https://github.com/HarperFast/harper/pull/1554) — Kris Zyp / Harper
Harper has an open PR generated by Claude Fable 5 that adds a `system.hdb_secret` table plus six super-user operations for a replicated envelope-encrypted secret store. The body is unusually specific about the security model: plaintext values are immediately encrypted against custody keys, submitted envelopes are structurally validated rather than decrypted, `kid` is derived from the sealed body, and secret operations avoid op replication because rows already replicate through system-table replication. A cross-model review found no blockers but did surface real pre-fix issues, including grant atomicity, MCP audit leakage of `value`/`values`/`envelope`, `read_audit_log` exposure of secret table record images, and duplicate grants; the branch now spans 19 files, 1,622 additions, and 72 passing touched-suite tests.

### [A small Metal tile cuts q4_0 batch-eight work in half](https://github.com/ggml-org/llama.cpp/pull/25377) — discobot / llama.cpp
A llama.cpp PR assisted by Claude Fable 5 targets a narrow Metal performance problem: the existing 64×32 `mul_mm` tile zero-padded 75% of the batch dimension at batch size 8 while `mat-mv` kernels scaled roughly linearly with batch size. The patch routes q4_0 × f32 to a 64×8 tile for batch sizes 5 through 16, touching three Metal backend files. The author reports a 2× improvement at batch 8 on an M4 Pro for `test-backend-ops perf 4096x14336`, a 19% end-to-end pp8 speedup on `gemma-4-26B-A4B q4_0`, and no effect on batch-1 decode.

### [Texera upgrades Iceberg to clear parquet-avro CVEs](https://github.com/apache/texera/pull/6208) — Yicong Huang / Apache Texera
Apache Texera has an open PR generated by Claude Code with Claude Fable 5 that upgrades Iceberg from 1.7.1 to 1.9.2 in `common/workflow-core` to resolve two parquet-avro Dependabot alerts, including CVE-2025-30065 and CVE-2025-46762. Instead of force-pinning parquet under an older Iceberg, the branch takes the smallest Iceberg release whose official dependency set reaches parquet 1.15.2, then regenerates four binary license and notice manifest sets for rebuilt services. One Scala source change adapts `IcebergTableWriter.flushBuffer` to Iceberg 1.9’s writer API, with a new unit spec covering flush-on-close, batch auto-flush, `removeOne`, and file prefixes; the PR says `sbt WorkflowCore/test`, Iceberg integration specs, strict binary-dependency checks, and notice generation all pass locally.

### [Internal M2M endpoints move off Mitos’s public console mux](https://github.com/mitos-run/mitos/pull/742) — stubbi / Mitos
Mitos has an open Claude Fable 5 PR for part of advisory GHSA-rcf5-cfv3-jxvv after hosted-deployment testing found bearer-gated `/internal/*` machine-to-machine routes mounted on the public console mux. The risk was concrete: `/internal/identity/resolve` provisions accounts and returns organization membership, so a leaked bearer would make account creation and org enumeration internet-exploitable. The patch adds a dedicated `--internal-addr` listener on port 8091, rewires Helm services and in-cluster resolve URLs, documents the threat-model delta, and adds tests that the internal mux serves routes behind bearer auth while unset-token configurations return 404 rather than failing open.

### [A construction CRM gets a 30-commit quality pass](https://github.com/jesse8393/fieldhorse-v2/pull/201) — Jesse / fieldhorse-v2
fieldhorse-v2 has an open Claude Code/Fable PR that reads like a full product hardening sprint rather than a single feature. Across 30 commits, the branch fixes misleading money-screen fallbacks, replaces 11 browser confirm popups, rate-limits public token endpoints, repairs tenant isolation on `fh_public_links`, adds real crew labor cost via per-member rates, builds desktop master-detail rails for jobs, leads, and quotes, finishes daylight-mode parity for field use, and consolidates repeated UI primitives. The PR reports every commit gated by typecheck, lint, 110 tests, and build, and later commits add hermetic visual-tour scripts plus interaction-state sweeps before pinning Claude Code sessions in the repo to `claude-fable-5`.

### [Eleven merged PRs from one Fable worktree sprint](https://x.com/DeVillefor/status/2074284327089979878) — DeVillefor
DeVillefor described a one-day Claude Fable 5 coding sprint that merged 11 pull requests from a single conversation thread after a month where 20–30 Opus 4.8 and GPT-5.5 PRs had remained partly finished. The practical technique is the interesting part: spawn proposed fixes into isolated git worktrees, time how long Fable takes to implement and verify them, then treat a two-minute fix very differently from a 90-minute scroll-bug slog. He says many branches never merge; their value is the observable signal about whether the model actually understood the change before a human pulls the successful work back together.

### [A refusal bug hid a zero-idea research pipeline](https://github.com/KeyAIGit/-ecdlp-lean-verification/pull/102) — KeyAIGit
KeyAIGit found that four runs of an elliptic-curve-discrete-log exploration pipeline were not failing because the math was dry; the Fable breadth tier was returning `stop=refusal` with zero content, and the wrapper treated that empty string as a successful answer. The fix makes refusal or empty completions fall through to cheaper models, logs stop reasons, block types, token counts, spend, and breadth-funnel counts, and turns extended thinking off by default after it also produced thinking-only max-token completions. A representative run now costs about five cents, finishes under a minute, and reaches the honest outcome: 8 ideas, 3 SymPy-supported checks, 0 leads after the Opus gate.

### [A CAN bus converter ships through five Fable-built releases](https://github.com/sdrdx4100/canbus-dbc/pull/1) — sdrdx4100
sdrdx4100 opened a Fable co-authored Rust desktop app for converting Vector BLF logs plus DBC definitions into CSV or Parquet. The branch includes a streaming BLF parser for compressed and stored containers, CAN FD variants and boundary-spanning objects; a DBC parser for endian modes, signed values, multiplexing and float overrides; bounded-memory exporters; an egui GUI; and a CLI path. The PR reports 19 tests plus a 10-million-frame, 75 MB BLF conversion in about 1.6 seconds with 4 MB peak RSS, then follows through release tags up to v0.5.0 with resampling, queue conversion, signal selection, empty-column dropping, and J1939 PGN matching.

It also refreshes the prompt and config for model routing and subagent delegation, with tests for request sanitization, provider routing, and trim safety.

The branch restructures the README and architecture docs, adds a Jest capture proposal, then implements an `rn-quick-render-jest` package, a verify subcommand, React Native version fixtures, and capture-normalization work after a Fabric spike was marked “GO.” Across 56 files and more than 10,000 additions, the PR turns prior phase notes into a user-facing package and test harness rather than leaving the renderer as project-internal research.

### [Five audits turn up stale MCP search and fifteen memory-system bugs](https://github.com/amart-builder/jarvis-memory/pull/23) — amart-builder
jarvis-memory has an open Claude Fable 5 overhaul based on five parallel audits of the whole project. ### [A screenplay test reporter stops marking interrupted runs green](https://github.com/NeoCognitus70/hand-baked-screenplay-pattern/pull/20) — GBrooks1970 / hand-baked-screenplay-pattern
A Fable 5 review of hand-baked-screenplay-pattern produced a small but concrete reporting fix: when a scene started but never finished, the old fold left the placeholder success outcome in place, so a crashed run could render as passed with 0 ms. ### [A literal GitHub Actions example blocked fleet-wide deploys](https://github.com/intelligent-group/.github/pull/33) — MRoot2025 / intelligent-group
While running a live Playwright QA gate against production for the first time, a Fable co-authored investigation found that recent app fixes were not actually deployed. The culprit was a composite action description containing a literal `runner.name` expression example; GitHub evaluates expressions inside `action.yml` metadata descriptions too, where the runner context is unavailable, so every workflow using the action failed at setup for more than ten consecutive deploy runs. The fix rewrites the description without expression syntax, verifies YAML parsing and the remaining expression markers, and ties the breakage to six merged fixes that had been stranded on `main`.

### [Real Canadian tax provisions stop losing to synthesized stubs](https://github.com/TheAxiomFoundation/axiom-foundation.org/pull/109) — PavelMakarchuk / The Axiom Foundation
The Axiom Foundation's Fable co-authored fix catches a data-selection bug in a legal-policy site. When a navigation leaf had both a real corpus provision and an encoded rule summary at the same citation path, the renderer returned the synthesized RuleSpec leaf and ignored the captured provision, so pages such as Canada’s 2025 alternative minimum tax showed a 190-character summary instead of roughly 27,000 characters of form text. The patch routes leaf resolution through the provision loader first, preserves the rulespec-only fallback for corpus-less jurisdictions, and adds a focused tree-node-loader test.

### [Canada corpus sectioning becomes a reusable ingest gate](https://github.com/TheAxiomFoundation/axiom-corpus/pull/250) — PavelMakarchuk / The Axiom Foundation

### [Closing and reopening a PR no longer bypasses a schema gate](https://github.com/block/schemabot/pull/641) — aparajon / Block
Block's schemabot PR fixes a specific GitHub workflow escape hatch: after a database apply had run, closing and reopening a PR could delete the stored `action_required` check and let the reopened PR converge to a passing gate even though the live database no longer matched the diff. The Fable-assisted branch keeps apply-owned blocking rows across close events, reattaches them to the new head on reopen, and only drops cleanly successful rows on merged closes. A reviewer found a narrower success-row race in the first version; the branch now retains success rows on unmerged closes too, with storage and webhook tests covering the bypass.

### [A semantic test matcher fixes cache behavior and partial-run durability](https://github.com/JustasMonkev/semantic-test-matcher/pull/2) — JustasMonkev
semantic-test-matcher's Fable co-authored PR attacks the slow path in a test-selection CLI rather than adding a new model prompt. The embedding cache is loaded once per run and flushed atomically under a cross-process lock, replacing a per-embedding read/lock/rewrite cycle that made match and benchmark runs behave like O(N²) cache I/O. Candidate embeddings now run concurrently, the first Hugging Face pipeline load is shared, transient Ollama failures retry before fallback, interrupted runs still flush completed embeddings, and the CLI reports progress, elapsed time, cache hits, and friendly top-level errors; new node:test coverage covers the cache store, retry logic, and concurrency helper.

### [Embedded IPython shells let nested scopes see caller locals](https://github.com/ipython/ipython/pull/15289) — Carreau / IPython
IPython has an open Fable-authored PR for a long-standing embedded-shell scoping edge case. Code typed into `IPython.embed()` is compiled as module-level code, so lambdas, comprehensions, generators, and functions defined inside the shell could raise `NameError` when they referenced locals from the frame that opened the shell. The fix installs a dict-subclass globals namespace that resolves reads through caller locals before module globals and propagates shell-defined global assignments back on exit, with new tests in `tests/test_embed.py` covering the nested-scope cases.

### [GitHub review suggestions stop deleting unrelated lines](https://github.com/parkerbxyz/suggest-changes/pull/157) — parkerbxyz / suggest-changes
suggest-changes has an open Fable-authored rewrite of the logic that turns diffs into GitHub review suggestions. The old heuristic grouping could make pure insertions without leading context delete existing lines when accepted, and its line-movement detector could corrupt unrelated edits whenever a common line such as `}` appeared in both the deletion and insertion sides. The new mapper segments each hunk into maximal contiguous edit runs, emits exact suggestions from those runs, skips additions to empty files that cannot be anchored, and adds tests for blank lines, edit runs, fixture application, review-comment limits, pagination, Windows direct execution, and dist verification.

### [A 500k-file FLAC browser avoids metadata-sort lockups](https://github.com/SuzukiDaishi/waves-previewer/pull/9) — SuzukiDaishi / waves-previewer
waves-previewer has an open Fable-authored performance fix for very large audio libraries. Sorting a 500,000-file FLAC list could enqueue one full decode per row in a single frame, while each metadata sort cost about 1.7 seconds in release builds and a second hidden sort could fire as the first metadata batch arrived. The patch streams sort-prefetch work under the existing per-frame budget, avoids full decodes for header-answerable keys, debounces streaming re-sorts, caps visible-row decode backlog, streams CSV export metadata jobs, and reports the main sort path down to about 0.55 seconds with regression coverage in the large-list and bulk-workflow tests.

### [ORC readers get two small malformed-file guards](https://github.com/apache/orc/pull/2671) — dongjoon-hyun / Apache ORC
Two draft Apache ORC PRs generated by Claude Fable 5 close narrow robustness gaps in the file readers. The C++ patch rejects compressed chunks whose advertised length exceeds the configured compression block size, matching a check already present in Java; the Java-side [companion PR](https://github.com/apache/orc/pull/2672) validates PostScript tail lengths before `long` values are cast to `int`, so malformed `2^31`, `2^32`, or `UINT64_MAX` lengths fail with `FileFormatException` instead of bogus offsets or allocations. Both are framed as defense-in-depth rather than CVEs and each adds a focused regression test.

### [nerdctl implements Docker v25 recursive read-only mounts](https://github.com/containerd/nerdctl/pull/5043) — Akihiro Suda / containerd
A containerd maintainer opened a Claude Fable 5-assisted nerdctl PR adding Docker v25-compatible recursive read-only bind and volume mounts. The implementation covers `bind-recursive` modes, runtime feature detection via `$RUNTIME features`, XDG-cache invalidation when the runtime binary changes, deprecation of nerdctl’s older `rro` syntax, and erroring rather than silently degrading when forced RRO is unsupported. The patch touches 15 files, including Linux, Darwin, FreeBSD, Windows, and OCI-runtime test coverage.

### [Camera reconnects move inside RTSP, MJPEG, USB, and simulated devices](https://github.com/zauberzeug/rosys/pull/423) — Niklas Neugebauer / rosys
rosys is using Fable 5 as a review and architecture voice on a camera reliability PR that keeps devices connected through network glitches, bad cables, and power hiccups. Instead of forcing a provider-level reconnect API, each device owns a self-healing capture loop: RTSP and MJPEG retry until shutdown but stop on credential failures, USB reopens and re-resolves `/dev/video*` nodes after disconnects, and the simulated device gains disconnection behavior for tests. Fable’s PR comments explicitly recommend this architecture over the earlier provider wrapper and discuss landing order across the current PR queue.

### [A Fable API integration fails until temperature is omitted entirely](https://github.com/expectedparrot/edsl/pull/2508) — John Horton / expectedparrot
EDSL hit a concrete integration failure with Claude Fable 5: every call returned `400 invalid_request_error` because the Anthropic service always sent a `temperature` field, and Fable rejects that parameter even when it is set to `1.0`. The PR adds model-family detection so Fable, Mythos, Opus 4.7+/4.8, and Sonnet 5 omit `temperature` entirely while older models keep their existing behavior. ### [A Tesla dashboard stops hanging on Railway startup failure](https://github.com/yerry262/Tesla-Dashboard/pull/5) — yerry262 / Tesla-Dashboard
Tesla-Dashboard merged a small Claude Fable 5 co-authored production fix for a live page that stayed on its loading spinner. The PR traces the failure to `uuid` v14 being ESM-only while the CommonJS backend booted on Railway’s default Node 18, crashing with `ERR_REQUIRE_ESM` and leaving `/auth/status` pending. The patch replaces the dependency with `crypto.randomUUID()`, asks Railway for Node 22 through `engines.node`, and gives axios a 30-second timeout so an unreachable backend falls through to the login page instead of spinning forever.

StarkWare has an open Fable co-authored echonet stack for replaying stored Starknet blob data through the OS as part of a monitoring report. ### [Fable ties Opus on VulcanBench while costing more and refusing tasks](https://x.com/morganlinton/status/2074499711848034445) — Morgan Linton / VulcanBench
Morgan Linton published a VulcanBench run comparing Claude Fable 5 and Claude Opus 4.8 on 15 real merged pull-request tasks, with low- and high-effort settings for each model. On the 13 common tasks all four configurations tied at 7/13 pass@1, while Fable runs cost about $22–26 and took roughly 99–104 minutes versus Opus at about $7–13 and 37–54 minutes. The hard-tier breakdown was worse for Fable high effort, which exhausted its output budget and wrote no code on the five frontier-hard tasks, and Fable also refused one or two legitimate networking tasks that Opus handled.

### [A compact hook mistook 187k Fable tokens for a full context window](https://github.com/affaan-m/ECC/pull/2468) — girish-kanjiyani7 / ECC
ECC’s strategic-compact hook had a Fable-specific context-window bug: `claude-fable-5` at 187,000 tokens was treated as a 200,000-token model, so the hook reported roughly 93% context use when real use was about 19% of Fable’s one-million-token window. The PR adds known large-window model-family detection for Fable and Mythos, keeps environment overrides first, and anchors substring matching so future suffixes such as a hypothetical mini tier do not inherit the one-million-token budget by accident. Five new tests cover the original Fable repro, Mythos, dated or region-prefixed IDs, override precedence, and unknown-model fallback; the author reports 2,976 tests passing with ESLint clean.

### [A granular synth adds pitch-synchronous grains after the stochastic path failed](https://github.com/Lifted-Truck/Auricle/pull/15) — Julian Smith / Auricle
Auricle’s merged Fable co-authored PR adds a Pitch Lock mode after small, high-density stochastic grains proved unusable noise. The new mode makes grain emission pitch-synchronous — `baseHz·2^(pitch/12)` — latches the read window to fixed buffer content, and uses constant-overlap-add gain so tiny grains form a tone instead of a cloud. The author says autocorrelation verification tracks C2 through C4 within about 15 cents, amplitude ripple has coefficient of variation around 0.03, 37 tests pass, and pluginval strictness 8 passes.

### [DeployEx engine restarts stop turning into monitor crash loops](https://github.com/thiagoesteves/deployex/pull/242) — thiagoesteves / DeployEx
Thiago Esteves opened a four-PR Claude Fable 5 fix set for DeployEx engine and monitoring edge cases: [initial-boot rollback timeouts](https://github.com/thiagoesteves/deployex/pull/239) no longer corrupt engine state, [cache writes](https://github.com/thiagoesteves/deployex/pull/240) become synchronous so immediate reads do not see stale UI settings, [stderr logs](https://github.com/thiagoesteves/deployex/pull/241) are streamed and retained instead of silently dropped, and [engine restarts](https://github.com/thiagoesteves/deployex/pull/242) tolerate already-running monitors instead of MatchError crash loops. ### [A local anime-data editor gets optimistic-save guards](https://github.com/NathapolDev/AnimeSubThaiOnYoutube/pull/23) — NathapolDev / AnimeSubThaiOnYoutube

The important guard is a per-entry content hash: if the pipeline rewrites an entry between load and save, the editor returns a 409 instead of overwriting newer generated data, and deployment explicitly excludes the admin UI.

### [PCB agents now report the design-rule damage they create](https://github.com/ecto/vcad/pull/438) — ecto / vcad

### [Nested dict ingestion becomes a planned Fable implementation series](https://github.com/kolodkin/aaiclick/pull/359) — kolodkin / aaiclick
aaiclick’s open PR shows a 17-commit Claude Fable 5 session moving from design spec to implementation for nested data ingestion. Follow-up commits handle nulls at every list level, reject `None` inside list-of-dicts, infer all-`None` values as nullable strings for cross-backend use, and consolidate the behavior into the user guide.

kolodkin’s samples PR is a 13-commit Claude Fable 5 run that starts with a design spec and TDD plan for a 3D wave-defense archery game, then builds the game in small slices. The branch adds a no-build Three.js scaffold with Playwright boot testing, seeded forest/desert/iceberg stages, first-person bow draw, ballistic arrows with trajectory hints, melee and ranged enemies, elemental arrows, wave spawning, ammo drops, stage progression, localStorage best scores, and a Preact HUD. ### [A trading bot branch keeps changing after walk-forward checks fail](https://github.com/SivanSoran/logic-task-pass/pull/1) — SivanSoran / logic-task-pass
logic-task-pass has an open Claude Fable 5 co-authored branch that reads like an iterative trading-system lab rather than a single scaffold. It starts with a FundedNext-focused equity-guardian scalper, then shifts after GBPUSD 2024–2026 walk-forward results show breakout-only M30/M12 configurations outperforming mean reversion. Later commits move intraday strategies to H1/H4 swing timeframes because $5-per-lot commission plus spread made buffer-limited scalping uneconomic, add an ONNX-trained probability model with time-ordered train/validation/test splits, and finish with a three-scalper ensemble that self-silences losing systems through a Beta-smoothed EV gate.

### [Expo ArcGIS archives stop failing on Xcode phase ordering](https://github.com/alex-krassavin/expo-arcgis/pull/6) — bhamiltoncx / expo-arcgis
expo-arcgis has a Fable 5 co-authored fix for a release-build failure that only appears when another Expo plugin appends a tail script phase such as Datadog dSYM upload. The PR explains that `addBuildPhase()` placed the ArcGIS Embed Frameworks copy phase after the tail script, creating an Xcode dependency cycle where dSYM upload waited on the finished app and the app waited on the embedded framework. The fix moves Embed Frameworks immediately after Resources, extracts the pbxproj mutation into a tested helper, and reports three Jest tests passing on a real parsed project fixture; a later commit deletes a duplicate ArcGIS xcframework signature to fix archive exit status 70.

### [Twelve scratch scripts find ten sqlite-utils 4.0 blockers and bugs](https://simonwillison.net/2026/Jul/7/sqlite-utils-4/#claude-fable-5-helped-a-lot) — Simon Willison
Simon Willison used Fable 5 in Claude Code as a final release reviewer for sqlite-utils 4.0, asking it to inspect the changes since the last 3.x tag, read the changelog and upgrade guide, and write scratch scripts for every new v4 feature. He says GPT-5.5 wrote five scripts and found nothing especially interesting, while Fable wrote 12 scripts, identified four release blockers and ten additional issues, and produced a combined repro script. The reproduced failures included implicit transactions left open after failed writes, rejected write pragmas that still took effect, foreign-key column order mistakes, CSV inserts changing existing column types, and migration stop-before behavior applying too much.

### [Radio-astronomy window functions get a 1.25x axis-scaling bug fixed](https://github.com/HERA-Team/hera_pspec/pull/514) — vincentmackay / HERA-Team
HERA’s hera_pspec PR says parts of the work were done with Claude Fable 5, including vectorization and cleanup, but the result is a domain-specific scientific correction rather than a toy patch. The author found that IDR3.1.1a theory-release window functions used an FT-beam frequency grid at 97.66 kHz while data used 122.07 kHz, silently scaling the k_parallel axis by 1.25x. The branch forces FT beams onto the data’s exact channels, adds extraction/interpolation and out-of-range tests, vectorizes cylindrical binning by about 20x with a 1e-12 parity test against the old loops, and moves FT-beam/window-function production into two CLI commands.

### [Helion kernel dispatch cache moves an H100 benchmark past vLLM on every case](https://github.com/pytorch/helion/pull/3009) — yushangdi / PyTorch
A Fable 5 co-authored PyTorch Helion PR adds a fast dispatch cache to `Kernel.__call__`, avoiding full specialization-key recomputation on repeated calls while preserving the slower bind/autotune path for new argument shapes. The body spells out the safety invariant: the cheap key is strictly finer than the full specialization key, the cache is populated only after a successful slow run, and it is bypassed under TPU compile capture or unsupported argument types. On an H100 per-token group FP8 quant benchmark, the posted before/after table moves Helion from 8 of 24 wins versus vLLM to 24 of 24, with geomean speedup rising from 0.913x to 1.268x and torch_compile wins rising from 19 of 24 to 24 of 24.

### [A bounded-model-checking pass stops dropping assumptions between timesteps](https://github.com/llvm/circt/pull/10788) — leizaf / LLVM CIRCT
An LLVM CIRCT pull request marked “Assisted-by: Claude:Fable-5” fixes a verification bug in the VerifToSMT bounded-model-checking loop. The old pop/push structure discarded assertions from earlier timesteps, including `verif.assume` lowered to SMT asserts, so checks at step i could ignore constraints from steps 0 through i-1 and report spurious counterexamples. The patch moves assumptions and definitions into the enclosing assertion level while keeping property negations scoped per step, adds 101 lines across three files, and the circt-tests comparison reported no change to the broader test results.

### [Datasette turns eight modal dialogs into a public web component](https://github.com/simonw/datasette/pull/2820) — Simon Willison / Datasette
Simon Willison's open Datasette PR has a detailed "Fable 5 PR" block and Fable co-author trailers across the commit series. ### [PostHog gets a repair path for lost CDC replication slots](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog/pull/69049) — danielcarletti / PostHog
A PostHog data-warehouse PR says it was authored with Claude Code using Claude Fable 5 after debugging a broken CDC source whose UI showed schemas as completed while the replication slot was gone and schedules were paused. It also makes the broken state "absorbing" so late batch completions cannot repaint the source healthy, and the CI comments show PostHog's large test/reporting stack running against the branch.

### [A daemon tick stops dying on truncated issue lists](https://github.com/jleechanorg/dark-factory/pull/191) — jleechan2015 / dark-factory
A Claude/Fable-5 dark-factory PR fixes a real `daemon --once` crash from an agent pipeline: `br list --json` silently returned only the first 50 rows, so external-reference deduplication missed an already tracked GitHub issue and tried to create a duplicate bead. ### [GraphQL repeated-field validation drops from 5.2 seconds to 0.11](https://github.com/graphql-python/graphql-core/pull/270) — bcmyguest / graphql-core
A graphql-core PR discloses that Claude:fable-5 generated a denial-of-service mitigation for the `OverlappingFieldsCanBeMerged` validation rule. The patch deduplicates structurally identical repeated fields before the O(n²) pairwise conflict pass, while deliberately including printed directives in the fingerprint so `@stream` conflicts are not erased. The author reports a 3,000-field repeated-query validation case dropping from about 5.2 seconds to 0.11 seconds, with 693 validation tests and five benchmark tests passing.

### [LOTUSim sends absolute simulation time to xdyn instead of step duration](https://github.com/naval-group/LOTUSim/pull/35) — cmoron / naval-group
A LOTUSim PR assisted by Claude Fable 5 fixes a co-simulation time bug in the physics-engine interface. The request field `t` was carrying the raw Gazebo step duration in milliseconds, so xdyn treated every state as starting near the same small time and evaluated time-dependent forcings such as waves at a constant wrong timestamp. The one-line fix sends the plugin’s absolute simulation time in seconds instead, and the author reports a websocket tap over a close-hauled run where `t` advanced correctly across 3,708 frames while calm-water trajectories stayed identical.

### [Helion adds a direct Triton launch path with cache-key guards](https://github.com/pytorch/helion/pull/3010) — yushangdi / PyTorch
A stacked PyTorch Helion PR extends the Fable 5 co-authored dispatch-cache work with a `triton_direct_launch` fast path. After a specialization compiles once, repeat launches can call the cached Triton `CompiledKernel` directly, while scalar values, tensor dtypes, alignment bits, captured globals, device, warp/stage choices, and cooperative-launch settings are folded into the cache key so hazards miss back to the slow validating path. The posted H100 group-FP8 benchmark comment reports 22 of 24 wins versus vLLM at 1.253x geomean, 20 of 24 versus Triton at 1.592x, and 24 of 24 versus torch and torch_compile.

### [Certificate issuance attempts regain complete audit trails](https://github.com/letsencrypt/boulder/pull/8846) — beautifulentropy / Let’s Encrypt Boulder

### [SPARQ packs benchmark axes onto one self-terminating EC2 box](https://github.com/sparq-org/sparq/pull/1769) — jeswr / SPARQ

### [A Rust fuzzer becomes self-contained and differential](https://github.com/jmanchuck/rustsmith/pull/3) — jmanchuck / rustsmith
A Claude Fable 5 co-authored rustsmith PR turns the project from a generator into a more complete compiler-fuzzing harness. ### [Mitos clones sandbox pools so org namespaces can be isolated](https://github.com/mitos-run/mitos/pull/746) — stubbi / Mitos
Mitos used a Claude Fable 5 branch to close the missing piece in its per-organization Kubernetes tenancy plan. ### [PyTorch Inductor restores effect ordering after a distributed deadlock](https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/pull/189209) — d4l3k / PyTorch
A PyTorch Inductor PR authored with Claude Code and Fable fixes a subtle scheduler bug in `with_effects` lowering. Star dependencies were recorded under `bufN` buffer names while the scheduler looked them up under `opN` operation names, so effect-chain ordering edges silently disappeared; after simple overlap became default, compiled torchcomms graphs could hoist a blocking receive above its paired send and deadlock every rank. The patch changes the keying to operation names, adds a regression test that failed before the fix, and reports an end-to-end 4×H100 torchcomms run where the previously hanging fullgraph send/recv suite passed with 22 tests and 210 subtests.

### [nanoclaw query history learns to stay inside tool-result budgets](https://github.com/jbaruch/nanoclaw-core/pull/78) — jbaruch / nanoclaw-core
A `nanoclaw-core` PR marked `Author-Model: claude-fable-5` fixes a context-recovery helper whose JSON output could exceed the 25 KB tool-result budget it was meant to protect. The new behavior clips oversized row content first, then drops oldest rows with explicit `content_truncated`, `rows_dropped`, and top-level `truncated` markers, and it adds `--offset` paging because the old error message recommended batching that the CLI did not expose. The PR updates the skill contract and reports new tests for paging, row clipping, envelope clipping, and negative offsets, with ruff, pyright, and 35 pytest tests passing.

### [Conference-feed writers stop losing each other's updates](https://github.com/jbaruch/nanoclaw-conferences/pull/41) — jbaruch / nanoclaw-conferences
Another `nanoclaw` PR marked `Author-Model: claude-fable-5` fixes a race in conference CFP state maintenance. The existing temp-file plus `os.replace` discipline prevented partial `cfp-state.json` files, but two writers could still read the same old state and let the later complete write discard the earlier update. The branch adds a persistent sibling `fcntl.flock` lock file around all six read-modify-write scripts, leaves read-only consumers lock-free, maps lock timeouts to the tools' documented exit contract, and reports 300 pytest tests passing with new coverage for lock creation, contention, environment override, and a threaded lost-update regression.

### [Rocq retries failed typeclass searches only after preserving the green path](https://github.com/rocq-prover/rocq/pull/22228) — Jason Gross / Rocq
Jason Gross opened a Claude Fable 5-written Rocq PR for a typeclass-resolution regression that broke fiat-crypto on the current Rocq development image. The fix leaves the existing resolution fixpoint alone, but when best-effort resolution fails it retries once with closed goals ordered last, so later goals can instantiate evars without perturbing resolutions that already succeed. The PR records two earlier Fable designs that failed full CI — including stack overflows in downstream projects and goal-count drift — before the final three-file patch, a distilled regression test, a full local test run, and verification that fiat-crypto's `MontgomeryLadder.v` compiles again on both the older offending commit and current master.

### [Flux scheduling fixes a policy-dependent granule match bug](https://github.com/flux-framework/flux-sched/pull/1505) — milroy / Flux Framework
Flux Framework’s scheduler PR is explicitly described as a collaboration with Claude Fable 5 and fixes a resource-matching bug exposed by `first*` match policies. Multi-slot jobspecs over high-capacity resource vertices could under-match under dynamic exploration or over-count under static exploration because the code tested aggregate capacity against per-slot requests instead of packable whole-edge-group shares.
