### [Airflow Databricks auth adds a supplied-token OIDC path](https://github.com/apache/airflow/pull/69272) — kaxil / Apache Airflow
An Apache Airflow Databricks-provider PR adds a `federated_token_provider` connection extra: a trusted callable that mints a short-lived OIDC JWT in-process, which the hook exchanges through Databricks’ RFC 8693 token endpoint instead of relying only on a Kubernetes service-account token from disk. The async path offloads the provider call so deferrable operators do not block the triggerer event loop, whitespace-only returns fail locally, and higher-precedence credentials still win. A Databricks reviewer posted a real-workspace verification note — service-principal federation policy, locally signed RS256 JWT, `_get_token` and `_a_get_token` happy paths, authenticated API call, cache reuse, and invalid-token negative checks — and disclosed that the note was drafted with Claude Code using Fable 5 before human review.

### [PostHog deduplicates server-side distinct ID lookups per request](https://github.com/PostHog/posthog-js/pull/4093) — dustinbyrne / PostHog
PostHog’s Next.js SDK PR says it was authored with Claude Code using Fable 5, with the key approach coming from a verified research pass over Vercel’s Flags SDK. The change memoizes `getDistinctId` resolution in a request-scoped `WeakMap` keyed by Next’s `headers()` instance, so a layout, page, and server components calling `getPostHog()` in the same App Router render do not each repeat an I/O-backed session lookup. It keeps resolver functions independent, deliberately caches rejections so redirects rethrow consistently, leaves the Pages Router path unchanged, updates JSDoc away from recommending React `cache()`, and ships across a 23-file stack that also introduces the `createPostHog` server factory.

### [Kvrocks caps deeply nested Lua replies before they crash workers](https://github.com/apache/kvrocks/pull/3547) — git-hulk / Apache Kvrocks
A Kvrocks PR marked “Assistant-By Claude Fable 5” fixes a server crash path in Redis-compatible Lua scripting. `ReplyToRedisReply()` converted Lua return values into RESP with native C++ recursion after `lua_pcall()` returned, so a self-nested table could overflow a worker thread stack rather than hitting Lua’s own guard. The first Fable patch used `lua_checkstack()`, but a follow-up commit records that this still waited until roughly 8,000 frames and could miss small worker stacks; the branch now caps reply nesting explicitly, surfaces a top-level error, and adds a Go regression test in the scripting suite.

### [Apiome adds live faceted search over MCP catalog metrics](https://github.com/apiome/apiome/pull/4701) — KenSuenobu / Apiome
Apiome’s merged PR says Claude Code using Fable 5 implemented a faceted MCP catalog API and UI over data that previously existed only as rich metrics. The new `GET /v1/mcp/{tenant_slug}/facets` route supports AND-across-facets and OR-within-facet filtering across grade, transport, category, safety, complexity, protocol, health, visibility, and pagination, while returning live bucket counts from the same filtered set. The author reports 4,027 backend pytest tests, 5,160 UI tests, a green root build, and 33 live-dev-DB acceptance checks covering counts, sentinel buckets, empty results, visibility, tenant isolation, and pagination.

### [Nextcloud SSO stops crashing on late service connections](https://github.com/nextcloud/Android-SingleSignOn/pull/1023) — MiMoHo / Nextcloud Android-SingleSignOn
A Nextcloud Android-SingleSignOn PR discloses that it was developed with Claude Code on `claude-fable-5` and fixes a crash reported by host apps such as nextcloud/notes-android. If `NextcloudAPI#close()` ran before an asynchronous bind to `AccountManagerService` completed, the pending `ServiceConnection` stayed registered and later called `onConnected()` on a nulled listener, producing a main-thread `NullPointerException`. The patch tracks requested bindings, unbinds even before establishment, ignores stale connection callbacks, and adds three JVM unit tests for the regular flow, stale callback after close, and close-before-connected unbind path.

### [Airflow streams Kubernetes task logs instead of materializing hundreds of megabytes](https://github.com/apache/airflow/pull/69300) — jason810496 / Apache Airflow
An Apache Airflow KubernetesExecutor PR says Claude Code Fable 5 helped implement streaming logs for running pods, using the new `BaseExecutor.get_streaming_task_log` interface so log lines flow lazily into Airflow’s bounded accumulator. The author reports the benchmark from the parent design: serving a roughly 415 MB running-task log drops peak heap growth from about 2,093.9 MiB to 179.9 MiB, an 11.6× reduction. A related [configuration PR](https://github.com/apache/airflow/pull/69301) adds `running_pod_log_lines` so KubernetesExecutor users can control the tail-line cap instead of inheriting the previous hardcoded value.

### [SpecR exposes confidence and provenance for inferred document hierarchy](https://github.com/wrzonance/SpecR/pull/418) — thewrz / SpecR
SpecR’s Claude Fable 5 co-authored hierarchy-inference branch persists `{ signalUsed, agreed }` provenance per paragraph and derives 0–1 confidence metadata at read time instead of storing a score that would need migration when the formula changes. The PR surfaces `meta.inference` in REST and MCP responses, adds a hierarchy section to onboarding reports, keeps SEC-sourced specs explicit rather than suspect, and proves zero classification drift over a 703-file fixture corpus. The same run also produced a smaller [re-import fix](https://github.com/wrzonance/SpecR/pull/417) for a live-reproduced bug where re-uploading a withdrawn library master rebuilt content inside a tombstoned row and left the fresh parse invisible.

### [Cribbage Trainer deep-links complete analysis state](https://github.com/markafitzgerald1/cribbage-trainer/pull/646) — markafitzgerald1 / Cribbage Trainer
Cribbage Trainer’s Fable 5 co-authored PR turns the analysis URL into a full state contract rather than only a hand parameter. Links can now carry six-card deal order, dealer-or-pone role, selected discards, sort order, and seed, with strict-but-soft parsing that rejects wrong counts, bad cards, duplicates, and discards not in the hand without crashing the app. The branch documents the compatibility surface, ignores local `.claude` worktrees that had doubled Jest runs, and records review-driven fixes for comma decoding, role-only links, popstate races, and stable browser-history behavior; validation reached 71 Playwright tests and 440 Jest tests at 100% coverage.

### [Policy research reruns recover previously blocked New Zealand health sources](https://github.com/thecolab-ai/the-for-good-project/pull/798) — adam91holt / The For Good Project
Two Fable 5 re-research PRs in The For Good Project revisit New Zealand public-policy findings after a fetch-tooling upgrade removed earlier bot-blocked-source caveats. The mental-health [rerun](https://github.com/thecolab-ai/the-for-good-project/pull/798) directly reads Budget 2025 material, the Beehive 111 crisis-response release, RNZ line items, Health NZ service-use data, and Te Hiringa Mahara monitoring, upgrading the “no published national community bed count” finding while saying an OIA is still needed for the precise number. The HPAI [rerun](https://github.com/thecolab-ai/the-for-good-project/pull/797) fetches MPI’s 22-page One Health strategy in full and concludes that the public flagship document still provides no sized wild-bird surveillance design, site list, seasonal frame, detection probability, or escalation trigger.

### [A relay cache gets a global memory budget and live-edge pinning](https://github.com/moq-dev/moq/pull/2110) — kixelated / moq-dev
A moq-dev PR co-authored by Claude Fable 5 tackles relay memory growth in `moq-net`: non-latest media groups were cached per track with only a TTL, so memory scaled with track count and would become unbounded if TTLs rose for FETCH. The patch adds a process-wide LRU byte budget where eviction aborts groups, wakes parked readers, pins each track's latest group, and accounts for late frames plus small groups. The commit trail also shows Fable fixing review and CI-discovered edges — repinning refetched latest groups, honoring eviction on the in-place frame-read path, and adding diagnostics for Linux-only eviction-order failures — while later refactors in the same branch are clearly attributed to Opus rather than Fable.

### [A TypeScript checker clone closes literal-display parity gaps](https://github.com/tsz-org/tsz/pull/15633) — mohsen1 / tsz
The `tsz` checker has another Fable 5 compatibility pass aimed at matching `tsc 6.0.2` diagnostics rather than just accepting the same programs. This PR generalizes failing literal sources the way TypeScript does across union, enum-member, tuple, property, array-element, return-type, overload, and top-level relation surfaces, with solver changes for instantiable constraints, lazy applications, conditionals, substitutions, and boolean unit pairs. The body lists each witness gap verified against `tsc --noEmit --strict --pretty false`, and the seven commits carry Claude session trailers through fix and simplification passes.

### [An economics paper adds machine checks after five simulated referee reports](https://github.com/PolicyEngine/llm-econ-beliefs/pull/7) — Max Ghenis / PolicyEngine
PolicyEngine’s `llm-econ-beliefs` paper used a Fable co-authored revision round to reconcile prose with regenerated 17-model tables after five simulated RSOS referee reports. The merged PR re-derives every ranking superlative, including a new place for Claude Fable 5 as the tightest labor-tax model, fixes stale constants and statutory anchors, clarifies panel counts and model budgets, and rerenders the paper. More importantly, it adds `scripts/verify_paper_prose.py` with 27 checks that assert the headline numbers and model-name superlatives against committed tables, alongside 71 passing pytest tests and rendered HTML/PDF spot checks.

### [A Unity XR provider fixes a macOS built-player input trap](https://github.com/DisplayXR/displayxr-unity/pull/214) — dfattal / DisplayXR
DisplayXR merged a Fable 5 co-authored fix for a macOS Unity-player bug where the provider opened a separate weave window while Unity’s real, tiny game window still owned mouse and keyboard input. The patch completes the in-app weave path: built players now attach an input-transparent overlay `NSView` to Unity’s own window, grow it to the display aspect, keep the editor preview path separate, and tear down whichever target was used. The author verified it in a BiRP CubeTest built player with a single correctly titled window, working stereo and focus, user-confirmed input, and a passing MinGW Windows cross-check.

### [Obsidian live sync starts materializing renamed notes again](https://github.com/engram-app/Engram-obsidian/pull/196) — Rasbandit / Engram
Engram’s Obsidian sync PR, co-authored by Claude Fable 5, starts from a deterministic end-to-end failure: after a rename broadcast, a receiving device recorded `received=yes` but never wrote the renamed note to disk because the WebSocket event carried no content change and CRDT enrollment was a no-op for an already-seen note. The fix first flushes the already-synced CRDT document to the new path, then a follow-up commit handles the fresh-boot case by copying trustworthy old-path disk content and ignoring stale backwards relocation events. The PR records red/green e2e evidence for `test_10`, a related echo-suppression fix, and new failing-first unit tests for both remaining rename-family bugs.

### [Harper tests HTTP/2 over a cleartext Unix-socket mirror](https://github.com/HarperFast/harper/pull/1707) — kriszyp / Harper
Harper’s experimental HTTP/2 ingress work was drafted with Claude Fable 5 and paired with a companion [symphony proxy PR](https://github.com/HarperFast/symphony/pull/24). The Harper side adds a flag-gated h2c Unix-domain-socket mirror that reuses the existing request and throttle pipeline, consumes an optional PROXY v1 header before handing the socket to Node’s HTTP/2 server, and drains live sessions with GOAWAY on close. The PR body reports benchmark work behind the design: translating h2 to h1 in the proxy cost roughly 25–30% more CPU end-to-end, while the direct h2c mirror measured 18.2 µs of CPU per request against 10.2 µs for the h1 mirror; the proxy side then dispatches by ALPN while rejecting h2 configurations that would corrupt the connection preface.

### [A profiler-fed Claude pass cuts pytest overhead on tiny tests](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/pull/14687) — Henry Schreiner / pytest
Henry Schreiner profiled pytest on pypa/packaging’s roughly 62,000-test suite with Python 3.15’s sampling profiler, fed the report to Claude, and credited the resulting patch as `Assisted-by: ClaudeCode:claude-fable-5`. The first optimization it found was in `FDCapture.snap()`: when a captured temp file is empty, a single `fstat` can skip the old `seek/read/seek/truncate` cycle. Schreiner reports that this removes about six cycles per test across stdout and stderr capture phases and cuts total runtime for that suite by about 8%.

### [Grails adds latency injection to turn UI flakes into local failures](https://github.com/apache/grails-core/pull/15937) — jdaugherty / Apache Grails
A Grails PR prepared with Claude Code and Claude Fable 5 adds a `grails-testing-support-latency` module for deliberately slowing selected requests in functional tests. The new filter has configurable delay bounds, probability, URL patterns, and seeds, fails fast on invalid configuration, and ships with an example app plus documentation warning that it is testing-only support. The author’s verification covers 10 unit tests for bounds, pass-through, and config validation; two end-to-end tests against the latency example app; a clean code-style run; and a docs build with the new functional-testing guide section rendered.

### [AetherSDR traces a second-pan crash to an old Intel D3D11 swapchain path](https://github.com/aethersdr/AetherSDR/pull/4120) — jensenpat / AetherSDR
AetherSDR’s Claude Fable 5 co-authored fix starts from a reporter’s Windows 10 minidump on an Intel HD Graphics 520 machine, where adding a second panadapter crashed inside `igd10iumd64.dll` while Qt rebuilt a D3D11 swapchain. The patch avoids transient top-level reparenting for panes that stay docked, collapses splitter layout to one resize, and pins `QRhiWidget` color buffers to even-aligned device-pixel sizes so fractional UI scale does not hand odd texture extents to the driver. The author reports a clean RelWithDebInfo build, 76 passing ctests, a live FLEX-8400M macOS/Metal smoke, and a later reporter confirmation that one to four pans worked across UI scale settings without crashing.

### [tsz matches TypeScript’s generator-yield literal widening cases](https://github.com/tsz-org/tsz/pull/15634) — mohsen1 / tsz
The `tsz` checker’s merged Fable-attributed PR pays down the `generatorTypeCheck63.ts` conformance row by matching TypeScript 6.0.3’s treatment of fresh literals yielded from unannotated generators. The body walks through the structural rule, including why `yield 1` under an `IterableIterator<T | undefined, void>` contextual signature should widen to `number`, while `yield 1 as const`, annotated `const` references, and multi-literal unions should keep their narrower forms. Verification includes 14 new targeted tests, an A/B full checker run with no new failures, 114 generator/yield conformance cases, and declaration-emit differentials for the matrix in the PR body.

### [finterm global installs find their bundled docs again](https://github.com/finterm-ai/finterm-cli/pull/12) — jlevy / finterm-cli
A Fable 5 co-authored `finterm-cli` PR fixes a packaging bug that only appeared after global npm install: the executable symlink made the old `/dist` detection miss the bundled documentation, so `skill`, `docs`, `prime`, and `setup` fell back to in-repo placeholders or exited with `SKILL.md not found`. The shared resolver now starts from `import.meta.url`, then tries raw and realpathed script locations before the development fallback. The pack smoke test was extended to run from a neutral working directory and assert real bundled content plus a working `finterm setup`, giving the PR a red-green guard against the exact published 0.2.0/0.2.1 failure.

It renders system prompt, tool documentation, and dense history into compact PNG pages and wires the engine through single and stacked compression modes with fail-closed gates for vision support, model, transport, source format, and profitability. The author reports a converted-block reduction of about 10× tokens and 59–70% end-to-end on measured examples, fixes the inflation guard to bill image blocks by dimensions instead of base64 characters, and records 1,249 compression tests passing plus a clean core typecheck and production-file lint after switching from a local file dependency to the published package.

Every’s Compound Engineering plugin PR, marked with a Fable 5 badge, fixes a failure mode where generated `docs/solutions/` entries could turn conversation summaries into permanent project knowledge without checking the repository. The new flow requires source-line reads before behavior claims, prefers PR numbers over fragile SHAs, runs a bundled mechanical validator for paths, commits, links, scaffold text, and stale-checkout state, and uses a semantic validator in full and headless modes to quote source lines and check merge-state claims against remote truth. The author reports 1,848 Bun tests passing, 31 new validator tests, and behavioral evals improving from 11/17 to 17/17 assertions on planted traps.

### [Polars-CV fixes average-precision math and unsafe data imports](https://github.com/heshamdar/polars-cv/pull/27) — heshamdar / polars-cv
A Fable 5 co-authored `polars-cv` branch starts with two evaluation-metric bugs: VOC 11-point AP was overestimated when undetected recall thresholds were dropped from the denominator, and `bootstrap_pr_auc` compared an enveloped point estimate against raw trapezoidal bootstrap replicates. The same eight-commit session also fixes rotate/affine fusion using the wrong shape hints, contiguous-stride declarations after materializing kernels, unchecked blob-header arithmetic plus hostile stride spans, Arrow C-Data imports that ignored array offsets and nulls, `file://` local reads, and aligned buffer deallocation. The PR body and commit messages give worked failure modes rather than only broad “bug fix” summaries.

### [Mallard stops deleting its event history on extension restart](https://github.com/RedPandaMC/Mallard/pull/57) — RedPandaMC / Mallard
Mallard’s Claude Fable 5 co-authored PR fixes a VS Code extension lifecycle bug where `deactivate()` wiped `events.duckdb` and global persisted flags on every window close or extension-host restart. That defeated migrations, ingest watermarks, retention, and any history older than rotated source logs, so the fix makes `deactivate()` a no-op and leaves full deletion to the explicit “Prepare for Uninstall” command. The broader 11-commit branch also separates pure domain code from VS Code and Node dependencies, moves dashboard layout into config, adds attribution provenance, and keeps Codecov reporting every modified coverable line covered.

### [QuantEcon adds repeatable DiscreteDP benchmarks and matching Python guards](https://github.com/QuantEcon/QuantEcon.jl/pull/383) — oyamad / QuantEcon
A Fable 5 co-authored QuantEcon.jl PR adds a BenchmarkTools/PkgBenchmark suite for `DiscreteDP`, covering four fixed-seed model cases and nine operations so future changes can be compared with `PkgBenchmark.judge`. A companion Python [PR](https://github.com/QuantEcon/QuantEcon.py/pull/855) fixes edge cases found while reviewing the module against the Julia implementation: duplicate state-action pairs could silently corrupt a model, trailing no-action states could read out of bounds under Numba, `operator_iteration` returned the wrong shape at zero iterations, and `beta` validation happened too late. Together they show Fable being used both to establish a reproducible performance baseline and to close cross-language correctness gaps.

### [moor keeps raw terminal mode after cmd.exe and Node reset it](https://github.com/walles/moor/pull/444) — walles / moor
A Fable 5 co-authored `moor` PR fixes keyboard breakage caused by other processes sharing the same terminal. On Windows, `cmd.exe` reset console modes while running batch files or ending a pipe; on Unix, a `node ... | moor` pipeline could restore cooked mode after `moor` had gone raw, leaving keystrokes echoed and line-buffered instead of delivered to the pager. The fix reasserts the wanted terminal mode from the read loop at least every 100 ms, preserves unrelated console flags, avoids reasserting during intentional cooked-mode pauses, and adds logging plus docs for the reset path.

### [Elden Ring save picking moves from OS dialogs into game menus](https://github.com/Banon-Labs/er-effects-rs/pull/40) — chozandrias76 / er-effects-rs
An `er-effects-rs` branch with Fable 5 trailers replaces two Windows file-picker dialogs with in-game menus rendered through Elden Ring’s native profile-selection UI. The System→Quit picker becomes a directory browser inside a 10-row game window, while the startup missing-save path boots to the native no-save title menu, auto-opens the picker, validates the chosen save through the old BND4/SteamID pipeline, and reloads through the game’s own return-to-title state. The 27-commit history records reverse-engineering constraints, live no-save test failures, overlay fallbacks, save-source protection, and guard fixes uncovered while making the native flow usable.

### [Outline stops Redis cache clears from blocking the server](https://github.com/outline/outline/pull/12934) — tommoor / Outline
Outline’s Claude Fable 5 co-authored PR replaces a startup cache-clear path that used Redis `KEYS`, which blocks the event loop while scanning the entire keyspace. The new helper walks matching prefixes with incremental `SCAN` and deletes in batches with `UNLINK`, so discovery and memory reclamation avoid stalling other clients on large installations. The change is small — two files, 96 additions, and seven deletions — but includes CacheHelper tests for multi-page prefix clears and documents the failure mode directly in the commit trail.

### [Monad hardens a secondary raptorcast client against cold-start edge cases](https://github.com/category-labs/monad-bft/pull/3157) — xinyuan-dev / Category Labs
Category Labs’ `monad-bft` PR says it was generated using Claude Fable 5 and applies a focused hardening pass to the secondary raptorcast client. It bounds `pending_confirms` and `confirmed_groups` during cold start, checks validator membership on `ConfirmGroup` and `NoConfirm` messages, restores a missing waker call in `RaptorCastSecondary::poll_next`, expires far-future cold-start entries, and rejects overlapping group invitations from the same validator. The branch changes five files with 778 additions and 242 deletions, making the report substantive enough to understand both the protocol risks and the intended fixes.

### [QuantEcon flips eight DiscreteDP broken tests into fixes](https://github.com/QuantEcon/QuantEcon.jl/pull/385) — oyamad / QuantEcon
QuantEcon.jl’s follow-up DiscreteDP branch is co-authored by Claude Fable 5 and turns the `@test_broken` markers from the preceding review into passing regression coverage. The fixes stop `solve(ddp, v_init, ...)` from mutating the caller’s vector, make modified policy iteration respect a supplied `v_init`, reject out-of-range state and action indices instead of silently reattributing sorted pairs, preserve value element types in `s_wise_max`, remove a type-pirated three-dimensional array multiplication method, and tighten beta-one warnings and convergence checks. Four Fable-attributed commits also update the benchmark suite after the internal multiplication change and align the Julia behavior with the companion QuantEcon.py edge-case fixes.

### [ngx-signal-forms closes three pre-1.0 audit findings](https://github.com/ngx-signal-forms/ngx-signal-forms/pull/201) — the-ult / ngx-signal-forms
The `ngx-signal-forms` maintainer is using Fable 5 to turn promoted pre-1.0 audit findings into regression-tested fixes across the toolkit. The Vest-adapter PR fixes two concrete bugs: default `resetOnDestroy` could reset a module-scope suite while a sibling mount still depended on it, and an internal `'root'` sentinel collided with a real Vest field named `root`; the commit says both were covered by failing-first tests. Nearby Fable co-authored PRs also make a missing form context produce the intended dev-mode warning for [`strategy="on-submit"`](https://github.com/ngx-signal-forms/ngx-signal-forms/pull/199) and restore [`@ngx-signal-forms/toolkit/testing`](https://github.com/ngx-signal-forms/ngx-signal-forms/pull/200) as a real secondary entry point, reporting build, lint, and 1,203 toolkit tests passing while noting an unrelated browser-test environment failure on a clean base checkout.
